Changchun Railway Bureau Headquarters) and first carried out an encirclement exercise, then set up sentries, established a communication network, and prohibited pedestrians from passing through South Avenue. At 5 pm, they returned to the West Park area and conducted a joint infantry-artillery battle, aiming at our Changchun County as a target, opening fire and shelling it. For a time, gunpowder smoke filled the air, and the sound of cannons boomed, firing more than 500 shells in total, until 3 am the next morning. Over 2,000 mu of farmland near the city were trampled and destroyed. When the shelling began, the residents were terrified. Those inside the city fled outside the city, and those outside the city fled to distant places. It was not until the Japanese military shelling stopped that the frightened souls were calmed. Afterwards, the Jilin authorities ordered the Changchun County magistrate to investigate, and the Jilin Diplomatic Commissioner's Office protested, but the Japanese consul did not reply.

Also, at 6:30 pm on the 12th, Yang Fulin, a porter at the Changchun Post Office, was sending a friend to take the South Manchuria Railway train. Because he was eager to buy a ticket, he asked someone to buy it from inside. Three Japanese station policemen, Yamamoto and others, caught sight of this and accused him of disrupting order, twisting Yang and beating him violently. Yang's companions tried to persuade them, but they were also beaten severely, and the mailbags were torn open, dumping the mail on the ground. Finally, they fired a gun to intimidate. Saito, the Japanese stationmaster, also cheered from the sidelines, and only stopped when Yang and others were severely injured and unconscious. Zhang Hongjun, the director of the Changchun Post Office, came to negotiate after hearing the news, but did not get anywhere. He only managed to get Yang out and send him to the hospital, but his injuries were very serious and his life was in danger. The Changchun postal community is very angry about this and has reported to the headquarters to negotiate seriously with the Japanese side. (15th)

Liaoning Post Office

Second Batch of Heroin from Germany Seized

Provincial Government Consults Ministry of Foreign Affairs to Protest to Germany and Japan

Shenyang Correspondence: The Postal Administration previously seized a large quantity of heroin purchased by the Japanese Iinuma from Hamburg, Germany. On March 10th, it invited Chinese and foreign personnel and journalists to supervise the burning. Not long after, the Postal Administration again seized 239 pieces of heroin, which was more than double the previous amount. The style was similar to the previously seized mail, also sent from Hamburg, Germany, to the Japanese merchant Fmine in Changchun. The Postmaster Balidi immediately detained all of them and sent a letter to Shenyang Customs Commissioner She Naomen, enclosing a package of mail, explaining the discovery. She Naomen sent the original items to Diller, the Customs Commissioner of Shanhaiguan, for testing. Diller confirmed that they were indeed heroin. For the sake of prudence, he took half of the white items from the mailed items and sent them to Jianghaiguan for testing. The results were undoubtedly heroin. Balidi immediately reported to the Postal General Administration and requested instructions. He was instructed to hand it over to the customs for handling and sent another letter to Shenguan Customs Commissioner She Naomen to return it to his handling. After She reported to the General Customs Administration, he was ordered to handle it jointly with the Customs Supervisor. After receiving the order, She again found five packages from that year, sealed them tightly, and sent them to Jianghaiguan for testing to obtain a second confirmation. Then, he sent a letter to Shenyang Customs Supervisor and Fu Shuangying to discuss the method of destruction. Previously, Customs Supervisor Fu Shuangying had seized postal transport of drugs, and the Provincial Government decided to burn them. This matter is the same and should be submitted to the Provincial Government for approval. After the Provincial Committee decided, it ordered the previous case to be followed, and also informed the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to protest to the German and Japanese ministers. At the same time, it also ordered the special envoy to seriously negotiate with the German and Japanese consuls. Regarding the co-verification and preparation for destruction, the destruction committee was still organized by Chen Wenxue, Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Wang Jinghuan, Special Commissioner of the Eastern Provinces, Sun Xuchang, Chief of the Police Department, Zhu Shusheng, Chief Prosecutor of the High Court, Bai Mingzhen, Director of the Shenyang Public Security Bureau, Fu Shuangying, Supervisor of the Shenyang Customs, Li Dexin, Mayor of Shenyang, Wang Jiarui, Magistrate of Shenyang County, and Lin Chengxiu, Counselor of the Provincial Government, to take charge. It is said that when the items are burned, Chinese and foreign personnel and journalists will still be invited to participate in order to show caution. The location is still the public sports field along the Xiaohe River. (May 15th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang

Robbers Kill Police at Shengzi Temple, Yexie, Under the Jurisdiction of the County. Shengzi Temple in the southern part of Yexie, where Songjiang and Fengxian meet, was reported by the Tinglin long-distance telephone this morning (21st) to the county government, stating that a gang of robbers suddenly arrived at Shengzi Temple last night. The head of the police station of the town's public security police station heard about it and led a team of police officers to rush to the town to block them. They exchanged fire with the bandits. The chief patrol officer was killed, and another patrolman was shot and killed. After receiving the report, the county government immediately appointed Wang Jinsen, a clerk, Chen Rongchu, the police captain, and seven other team members, bailiffs, and forensic officials to take a convenient steamer to Shengzi to investigate.

County Party Department Bans Reactionary Publications. The Propaganda Department of the County Party Affairs Consolidation Committee previously sent personnel to investigate reactionary publications, of which there were dozens. Some changed the cover of textbooks to disguise themselves. There are many tricks, and if prevention and control are slightly neglected, they can easily be mixed in. Several kinds of "New Culture" publications were found in a local bookstore. The contents were all reactionary texts. Therefore, a meeting was convened today to talk to the managers of various bookstores. In the future, all new books must be reviewed before they can be sold. At the end, the department sent a table of reactionary publications to each manager for reference.

Suzhou

Summary of County Administrative Meeting: The County Government held a county administrative meeting yesterday (the 21st), chaired by County Magistrate Huang. The resolutions included: (1) A request for an additional temporary repair fund of 1,500 yuan for the silkworm farm was temporarily reserved; (2) The temporary collection of construction permits in the urban area, with an additional 20% for public security expenses, will continue as before.

New County Police Captain Takes Office Today: Du Hongyi (style name Yimin) was appointed as the new Captain of the County Police Brigade. After receiving the appointment, Du will take office today (the 22nd).

Robbery and Kidnapping by Bandits in Hengjing Township: In Hengjing Yanghejing Township, more than twenty bandits arrived the night before last (the 20th) and robbed the Xu Dechang tobacco and money shop, kidnapping the shop owner Xu Wenbin and carpenter Shen Jinyuan. The estimated loss is about three to four hundred yuan. After hearing the alarm, the Public Security Branch immediately ordered senior police officers to pursue the bandits, but they were not found.

Wanted: Hit-and-Run Driver: On the 25th of last month, Shen Jiren, who was driving a fire engine for the Nanhao Street Qiansu Neighborhood, Section 8 fire brigade, drove around on the road. Near the Guangji Bridge, he hit and killed Shi Peiquan, a coppersmith. The Wu County Court sent personnel to investigate. Later, Shen Delin, a member of the fire brigade, was detained and interrogated, but was found not guilty. The court ordered the fire brigade to pay Shi's wife, Zhang, a compensation of 1,000 yuan. However, Shen Jiren fled the scene immediately after the accident and has disappeared without a trace. The local court considers Shen Jiren a major suspect in the case, and has repeatedly tried to summon him, but he has not appeared. Yesterday (the 21st), the court sent a letter to all land and water public security agencies, ordering them to assist in arresting Shen and bringing him to justice.

Silk Shop Owner Hangs Himself: Sun Yangfeng, 52 years old, a shareholder and manager of Tianfengchang Silk Shop in Xizhong City inside Changmen, usually managed the store with great care, resulting in annual profits. In the past month, Sun suffered from mental strain, leading to occasional mental confusion. He consulted Dr. Fang Jiamo, who advised him to rest. However, Sun was stubborn and unwilling to let go of store affairs, leading to a severe deterioration of his mental condition. On the night of the 20th, Sun stayed alone in the upper floor of the store's warehouse. For unknown reasons, he became despondent, used hemp rope to tie up silk goods, and hanged himself from the bed. No one noticed that night. Yesterday (the 21st) at 8 a.m., when the store was opening for business, shop assistant Wu Hanchu went upstairs to get the key to the display window and found Sun hanging from the bed, dead. He called all the shop assistants upstairs, closed the shop, and informed Sun's wife, Chen, who came to the store to arrange funeral matters. The officer Bai of the North Third Precinct ordered the local constable, Han Runqing, to report to the local court to send someone for an inspection. His wife, Chen, and son, Yongqing, petitioned and were granted exemption from inspection. As for the store's affairs, since it was a joint venture, they would be reorganized after the funeral arrangements were made.

Kunshan

Execution of Bandits: Four bandits, including Zuo Zhengming, were arrested for robbing the home of Tao Ganbo in Laqitu, Bacheng Township. After investigation, they were executed by firing squad in March. Wang Anfu was ordered to be retried. After the county government received the order, it re-examined the case and still sentenced him to death. After being approved by the provincial government, on the morning of the 21st, County Magistrate Pang verified the identity of the criminal and had him tied up and taken to the execution ground at the foot of Ma'anshan for execution by firing squad.

Qingpu

Merchant Ship Robbed En Route: The Zhaoshang Yuqing small steamers, which have been running between Zhujiajiao and Shanghai for more than ten years, were suddenly robbed yesterday. The Zhaoshang steamer departed from Zhujiajiao and, when it reached about three miles from Ji Wang Temple, eight people in a ferry boat approached. Initially, they were thought to be passengers, but after boarding the ship, they pulled out pistols and prevented the ship from sailing. They searched all the passengers and their luggage. However, most of the passengers were laborers and did not have much to lose. Only a passenger surnamed [omitted] who was disembarking at Huangdu was said to be carrying 800 yuan in banknotes to a Shanghai bank, which was also robbed completely.

Zhang Ye Sues Her Husband: Zhang Ye, 30 years old, from the north gate of this city, claims her husband, Zhang Mingjun, works as a clerk in Zhenjiang and earns a substantial monthly income. They have been married for many years and have a son and a daughter. Recently, her husband married a concubine in Zhenjiang and lives separately. Zhang Ye is often treated coldly by her in-laws in Qingpu and does not receive any money for the children's clothes or expenses. She had no choice but to report the situation to the county party headquarters for help. The county party headquarters forwarded the letter to the Provincial Women's Federation for handling. The federation asked Zhang Ye to come to the province to explain the situation. After finding the case to be true, they summoned Zhang Mingjun and tried to persuade him. Zhang initially acted cunning, but after repeated persuasion, he agreed to provide Zhang Ye with ten yuan per month for expenses. Room and board would still be at the in-laws' house, and her husband would be responsible for medical expenses or additional expenses for the children. Zhang Ye was satisfied and returned to Qingpu the day before yesterday.

Wuxi

The Outcome of the Petition Regarding Municipal Funds and Assets: After the Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office was ordered to close, the municipal affairs were taken over by the relevant county bureaus. The Municipal Engineering and Donation Offices were also taken over by the Construction and Finance Bureaus, which assigned staff to start working. However, the management of municipal funds and assets has caused disputes. The County Party Consolidation Committee invited representatives from the First and Second District Party Headquarters and mass organizations to hold a joint meeting. They resolved to appoint representatives to go to the province to petition the party and government. Representatives from the County Party Consolidation Committee, District Party Headquarters, and the agricultural, labor, commercial, youth, women's consolidation committees, the Municipal Education Association, and the National Guidance Daily were appointed. On the 19th, they went to the province to submit a petition to the Provincial Government's Department of Civil Affairs, stating their wishes and requesting responses to three matters: (1) Whether Cao Hengzhi, Yang Hanxi, and others were petitioning the province in the name of citizen representatives; (2) Whether the province had given instructions regarding the Qichang charter; (3) The province's opinion on handling this matter. Chairman Ye and Director Hu expressed that Yang and others petitioned the province in the name of citizen representatives, advocating that the municipal affairs be returned to the First District Office for management and that a Municipal Asset Management Committee be formed. However, the province had already decided that the county would select impartial local people to serve on the committee and first draft a charter to be submitted to the provincial department for approval. Everything should be handled in accordance with the approved charter. If there are local bullies mixed in, not only can the citizens object, but the province will not approve it. In the future, a better plan should be devised to suit the local situation. The representatives expressed their satisfaction and left. They then went to the Provincial Party Headquarters, where various committee members met with them and stated that the party headquarters should conduct effective supervision. The candidates for the municipal asset management committee should be agreed upon by the local government and the party headquarters. They also advocated that citizens should organize a municipal research association to promote the city's development. The representatives followed these instructions and returned to Wuxi yesterday, actively organizing a municipal research association.

Scheduled Opening of the Wuxi-Cheng Bus Route: The Wuxi-Cheng Highway and the Wuxi-Cheng Bus Company are actively proceeding with the preparations for the opening of the road, as the entire project is nearing completion. Manager Feng Xiaozhong has purchased four baggage cars, four freight cars, and eight first- and second-class passenger cars in Shanghai. There will be ten round trips every day, starting with the Wuxi to Qingyang route on July 1st. The section north of Qingyang will be extended to Cheng after the bridges and road work are completed.

Strict Punishment for Opium Traffickers: In February of this year, the county government arrested Xi Changfu for trafficking in opium, along with evidence. It was also learned that Xi was a railway worker and that the opium transported from Shanghai to Wuxi was insured by Xi. After repeated interrogations, Xi initially denied the charges. Yesterday, Zhou, the investigating officer, summoned the senior police officer who carried out the arrest and other witnesses. After the evidence was confirmed, Xi Changfu was sentenced to three years in prison and fined 2,000 yuan. Establishment of the Municipal Donation Office: After the Wuxi Municipal Preparatory Office was ordered to be abolished, all affairs were transferred to the relevant bureaus. The Municipal Engineering Office has been established, and yesterday, Director Yao of the Construction Bureau also served as the director, appointing Yan Zhongying as the technical director, Zhang Mingou as the administrative director, Qin Xiangtao and Gu Yucheng as clerks, Zhang Zaiqu as an engineer, and Wang Xingzhi as an investigator. After receiving their appointments, all the staff have gone to their posts to handle affairs. The Municipal Donation Office was also established yesterday by Director Chen of the County Finance Bureau, with Chen serving as director and Qiu Jun as deputy director. Fu Jiantian was appointed as the accountant, and the remaining staff will remain unchanged for the time being. In addition, as a result of the local delegation's petition to the province, a municipal research association is being organized and is currently underway.

Sentencing of Rape and Kidnapping Offenders: Bao Xingyun, a 19-year-old female worker at the Six-Headed Workshop of the Shengyu Silk Factory in Yangming Township, was abducted by kidnappers Xu Bingshan and Jiang Laowu in April of this year. She was raped once by Xu Bingshan and planned to be sold in Shanghai. Railway police discovered the crime and transferred the three to the county government for interrogation. Later, two women, Xu Zhang and Xu Zhao, were also apprehended. Xingyun was sent to the Labor Hospital for examination to determine whether she had lost her virginity. The hospital sent a letter to the county government the day before yesterday, along with a certificate stating that the outer part of her lower body was bruised and her hymen was broken. Yesterday, the investigating officer Zhou opened the court and announced the verdict: Xu Bingshan was sentenced to eight years in prison for rape and three years in prison for abduction, to be served concurrently for a total of nine years and ten months. Jiang Laowu was sentenced to three years in prison for abduction. Xu Zhang and Zhao were acquitted.

Nantong

Appointment of Special Industrial Police Captain: The Department of Civil Affairs ordered the County Government to approve the resignation of Xu Zuhong, Captain of the Special Industrial Police Team of Tongtai Haiqi, and appoint Zhang Huan to replace him. Zhang has arrived in Nantong from the province and is scheduled to take over.

Lusi Pirate and Bandit Alert: More than ten pirate ships suddenly appeared off the coast of Lusi, robbing merchant ships and fishing boats. On the 20th, the pirates joined forces with bandits from Xinhe Town, and their activities were rampant. Because the eastern township's telephone lines were cut off by the bandits, the details are unknown. At 5:00 p.m., Qu District Chief of Lusi Cheng telegraphed the county government for help from the reclamation area. County Magistrate Zhang requested the Nine-County Bandit Suppression Command to send troops to suppress the bandits.

The Situation of Yudong Being Plundered by Bandits: Yudong Town, located 120 li east of the county seat, was suddenly looted by bandits at 6:00 a.m. on the 19th. The bandit gang, numbering over 600, carried over 300 rifles, submachine guns, and Mauser pistols. The bandits wore red headbands around their necks as a mark. They first went to the district office and public security bureau, searched the premises, and set fire to a portion of the buildings. Then, they robbed merchants and residents. The Ren Tai Pawnshop suffered the greatest loss. The telephone exchange equipment was completely destroyed, and over fifty telephone poles were sawed down. The bandit gang left with their loot around 10:00 a.m. Hu's battalion of the Fifth Division, stationed in Erjia Town, heard the alarm and went to suppress the bandits. On the morning of the 20th, they encountered the bandits at the Fenghuang Bridge, and both sides opened fire. More than ten bandits were killed, and two soldiers in Hu's battalion were also killed or wounded. In addition to dispatching county police to pursue the bandits, the county government also sent a commissioner to investigate and appease the local people. The provincial police team intercepted two key bandits at Wufu Bridge. The evidence was conclusive, and they confessed to the crime. They were taken to Erjia Town for execution by firing squad.

Danyang

Attempted Robbery Outside the West Gate: The area outside the West Gate of this city has always been a bustling rice market. Around 8:00 p.m. on the 20th, four bandits suddenly broke into the inner room of the Hua Dachang Grain Store with pistols, attempting to rob it. The military police arrived after hearing the news, and the bandits fled.

Japanese Privately Photograph Ancient Steles in the Park: The park in this city contains a rich collection of ancient bronzes and stone inscriptions. Yesterday morning, Japanese nationals Sekino Tadashi, Takutori Takeichi, and photographers privately photographed the Liangling Rebellion Stele. They also claimed they were going to Xiaotang Alley to search for ancient stone Qilin. The Public Security Bureau learned of this, sent personnel to check the Japanese nationals' passports, found them to be inconsistent, and ordered them to leave the country.

Zhenjiang

Minutes of the Shareholders' Meeting of the Da Zhao Electric Company: The Zhenjiang Da Zhao Electric Company held a shareholders' meeting yesterday at the office of the Dasheng Yarn Factory on Jiujiang Road. The shares represented at the meeting totaled 4,925 shares. The meeting began at 2:00 p.m., and Zhou Meiquan was elected as the temporary chairman. After the opening remarks, the supervisor reported on the previous year's accounts, followed by Guo Zhicheng, who reported on the company's business situation. They also discussed proposals and elected directors and supervisors. As a result, Zhou Meiquan, Xu Yu, Yuan Bo, Lu Xiaobo, and Guo Youting were elected as directors, and Ding Jiehou and Li Xibai were elected as supervisors. It was decided to convene a board of directors meeting the next day to welcome the new directors and supervisors.

Departure of the Propaganda Team of the Provincial Consolidation Committee: The propaganda department of the Jiangsu Provincial Party Affairs Consolidation Committee has organized two roving propaganda teams to expand propaganda efforts. The two teams departed simultaneously this morning. The first team will be responsible for 28 counties, including Nantong, and the second team will be responsible for 20 counties, including Tongshan. The two teams are scheduled to conduct propaganda for two months each, with two days of propaganda in each county. If there are special circumstances, the duration may be adjusted accordingly.

Yangzhou

Was the Constable Punished for Gambling? An Zheng, the director of the Public Security Bureau, dispatched inspectors Liu and Zhang to investigate the reports in the Yangzhou newspapers that Constable Yu Xuxiang of the Fourth Precinct had repeatedly discovered gambling dens outside the West Gate and punished the gamblers. They obtained written statements from those who were fined (totaling 14 yuan for four gambling dens and 45 yuan for four gamblers, including Zhao and Ma). On the 19th, the police chief summoned the heads of the police stations in the area and those who were fined for questioning, in order to investigate the matter.

Gaoyou

Bandits Pillage Sheyang Town, Baoying County: Several hundred bandits suddenly arrived at Sheyang Town, Baoying County, the day before yesterday. They carried two machine guns, seventy or eighty box cannons, and over a hundred rifles. They split up and looted everything, burning down many houses. They abducted dozens of men and women. The estimated loss is said to be between one and two hundred thousand yuan.

Gaoyou's Financial Sector Affected by Yangzhou: Three Qianzhuang (money shops) in Yangzhou suddenly went bankrupt, owing tens of thousands to banks and Qianzhuang in Shanghai, Nanjing, and Zhenjiang. It is now reported that a creditor group has been formed by the three cities to negotiate with Yangzhou and to send personnel to investigate whether the Qianzhuang in various counties north of the Yangtze River are solvent and reliable, so as to determine whether to continue doing business with them. The Qianzhuang in this county are now affected by the bankruptcy, and representatives from each Qianzhuang will discuss measures to maintain stability at the Qianye Guild Hall at 11:00 a.m. today (the 19th).

Jiashan

Caijiadou Village Completely Robbed: Twenty or thirty bandits arrived at Caijiadou, three li from Xitang Town in Jiashan, last night and robbed the village. The losses are said to be very heavy.

Hangzhou

Security Regiment Arrives in Jiande: The Zhejiang Provincial Government discovered that bandits had appeared in Jiande County, with a large number of them, and the situation was critical. It urgently dispatched the First Regiment of the Security Team to rush to Jiande to pursue and suppress the bandits. Yesterday, a telegram was received stating that the regiment had arrived in Jiande and had begun the encirclement and suppression. Some of the bandits had already fled, and they were still being pursued.

Deliberating on Opinions on Pacifying Taihu Lake: The Zhejiang Provincial Security Office received an order from the Provincial Government yesterday, instructing it to submit its opinions on the important points for pacifying Taihu Lake in this province and how the security team should be deployed in the future. Yesterday, it drafted a plan based on the situation of Taihu Lake on the Zhejiang side and the organization of the suppression and defense. It will be submitted to the Provincial Government soon to be forwarded to the Ministry of Interior and the Joint Bandit Suppression Commander of the three provinces for consideration.

Auditing the Budget of the Provincial Public Security Bureau: According to the newly compiled budget submitted by Yan Youfu, the Director of the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, the Director of the Department of Civil Affairs, Zhu Jiahua, has redivided the police area of the provincial capital into ten districts, with a branch bureau in each district. He is unsure whether the regular expenses are in line with reality, especially at a time when the provincial funds are scarce. Yesterday, he personally audited the budget and instructed the police administration section to draft a report for submission to the provincial government for approval.

Shangyu

Disputes Arise Again Over Shaoxing People Encroaching on Sand Land Across Borders: Since the 13th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, the Xiaonanhui sand land in Li Hai has been the subject of disputes among sand people over land ownership. The former County Magistrate Tang ruled that the land should be confiscated by the Jingzheng Academy. This was the beginning of the county's education fund. Later, in the 24th and 31st years of Guangxu, there were successive additions. County Magistrates Tang, Chu, and Ye gave licenses to the sand people who contracted to cultivate the land, and there was peace for decades. During the 9th, 10th, 11th, and 3rd years of the Republic of China, the sand land was eroded by floods, losing over a thousand acres. By the 13th and 4th years, the land had collapsed and resurfaced. The former Senate re-measured the land and issued licenses to the original contractors as usual. However, in the 15th year, Tong Rong, the director of the Shaoxing Reclamation Bureau from another county, sold over 600 acres of sand land in that area. In the 16th year, the political situation changed, and the Reclamation Bureau was renamed the Sand Field Bureau. Tong Rong managed to be appointed as the director of the Yu-Shang Sand Field Branch and illegally sold over 1,400 acres of sand land in that area. The buyers in both instances were Feng Meiyan, who used the pseudonym Yu Shengjie from Jiangkou, Shaoxing County, and Yi Jiachang and others from Xihui Zui. They forged documents and illegally planted signs across the border. At that time, all the local legal organizations in the county listed the evidence and telegraphed the province to fight for their rights. In the 17th year, the Yu-Shang Sand Field Branch established a Sand Field Office in Baiguan. The education fund association registered with the office, totaling over 2,000 acres of new and old land. In the spring of the 18th year, the Sand Field Bureau established an office in Li Hai Suo, and the education fund property association reported the measurement of the land. The previous registration and measurement, except for the undisputed 1,800 acres of old land that had not collapsed, showed that the 394 acres of new land were subject to disputes due to the over 2,000 acres sold by Tong Rong in two instances. As a result, our Yu County's educational public property suffered many disputes. The Ministry of Education, the Provincial Government, the National Zhejiang University, and the Departments of Finance and Education approved the investigation and found the claims to be true. Unexpectedly, on May 5th of this year, Feng Meiyan, Yi Jiachang of Shaoxing County, and Wang Fushun and other vagrants from Nanhui, along with armed police from the Sun Duan Public Security Branch, encircled 2,800 acres of dikes in the Xiaonanhui area. The original contractors were extremely indignant. They reported the matter to the County Education Fund Association, which requested the County Government to send police four times to stop them, but to no avail. On the 19th, over 130 original contractors, including Xie Jiyan, Chen Bingzhao, Wang Yuelai, and Chen Yuanying, were so angry that they could not contain themselves. They gathered at the county government and demanded that police officers be sent to repel the visiting police and that the provincial government be telegraphed to order the Shaoxing County Government to order the Sun Duan Public Security Branch not to interfere across the border in the future, so as to clarify the county boundaries and suppress the seeds of chaos.

Ningbo

Change of Director of the Huang Gu Lin Public Security Branch: The former Director of the Huang Gu Lin Public Security Branch in Yin County, Chen Shangli, was removed from his position after being accused of a case by someone in the province. It is now reported that the Department of Civil Affairs has appointed Ma Qi to replace him. He has arrived and taken office.

Tragedy on the Yin-Feng Provincial Highway: The Jiang-Feng section (from Jiangkou to Fenghua City) of the Yin-Feng Provincial Highway Bureau is scheduled to reopen on the 20th. However, there are still several sections of the road surface that need to be repaired. Around 8:00 a.m. on the 18th, over thirty road workers were using a road roller to roll the road surface at Xiang Ling, near Chang Ting Village. While going down the hill, one of the workers stopped to pick up a sunshade, causing the road roller to roll down freely, crushing three people to death. Two had their heads crushed, and one had his chest crushed. The three bodies were later collected by the road bureau.

Wuyuan

Banditry Occurs in Sikou Town: Yesterday (the 14th) at 6:00 p.m., a group of over thirty bandits, each carrying handguns, wooden clubs, and long knives, gathered at Niujiaowu outside Sikou Town in the north of the county. They entered the town through Xiaojie Street, firing their guns as a show of force. The merchants were having dinner when they suddenly heard the gunshots. The bandits were fierce, and everyone was panicking and at a loss. They fled in all directions. The bandits then proceeded to the upper street and looted the major shops, tying up the owner of Shun Chang Store and demanding money. They then went through Yujia Lane in the middle street and went straight to the home of Yu Xintian, a branch of the Hongyuan Yongwu Tea Shop. They broke down the door, rushed in, and searched everywhere, taking all the cash and family jewelry stored in the shop. They gathered at Shangdiantan, wrapped the loot in bundles, and shouted as they went to Yanchuan, Sixi, and Xichongyuan before heading south. After the incident, the store owners investigated the losses. The Yu Xintian family suffered the greatest loss, with an estimated total of over 30,000 yuan in cash, jewelry, and damaged items. The second-largest loss was at the Yi Tai Grocery Store, where 1,400 yuan in cash was robbed. The Ren Tai Cloth Store lost about 500 yuan in silk and foreign goods. Shun Chang Rice Store lost several hundred yuan. The other stores, including Tong Fayuan, Zhu Huatang, Shen Long, Yi Yuhe, and Yi Shengchang, all lost between a hundred and several dozen yuan. The shops on the lower street did not suffer any losses.

Hefei

Tragic News of the Family of Executed Bandit: Xu Dai, the biological mother of Xu Guorong, the bandit who was executed, Xu Tang, the adoptive mother, and Xu Guo, the wife, all attempted suicide by opium or gold ingestion due to the loss of their family. Xu's wife even tried to strangle her two daughters, but a Western doctor was called to rescue them. The poison was too strong, and they are all in critical condition. However, in addition to the Hong Shun Xiang Timber Company that Xu's family jointly opened with Wang Hanchen in Beiwai, there is also a timber company in Sanhe, as well as a lot of real estate and land, totaling tens of thousands of gold. Xu Guorong's brother, Guoliang, heard that the government was planning to confiscate the family property. He has asked all sectors to request that the confiscation be waived in order to maintain their livelihood.

The Entire Town of Gao Liuji Was Robbed: The town of Gao Liuji in the west was robbed clean by over a hundred bandits the night before last. No household was spared. Before leaving, the bandits set fire to the town, burning down most of the houses. People have been coming to the city to report the case.

Tokyo, May 21st (Special Dispatch from This Newspaper): Tonight at 7:00 p.m., representatives from the four countries spoke on the Tokyo Radio Broadcasting Station. Past Far Eastern Games have often ended unhappily due to trivial misunderstandings. Receptions by Two Organizations

Mitsukoshi Company

Tokyo, 21st - A telegram reports that Mitsukoshi Company held a welcoming reception at its upstairs lounge yesterday at 1 PM, inviting athletes from various countries participating in the Far Eastern Games. Energetic Japanese athletes, Chinese athletes wearing the Blue Sky with a White Sun flag on their chests, lively Philippine athletes, and Indian athletes participating for the first time, chatted around tables. The grand event concluded and the meeting adjourned at 3 PM.

Japanese Athletic Association

Mr. Seiichi Kishi, the chairman, as well as representatives Mr. Zhang Boling from China, Mr. Vargas from the Philippines, and Mr. Mookerjee from India, all delivered speeches. Great Excitement in Tokyo City

Competing to Purchase Tickets

Hotels Will Be Full

Tokyo, 21st - A telegram reports that the opening date of the 9th Far Eastern Games is fast approaching, and preparations for the stadiums and other facilities have been completed. Everyone is only waiting for the opening ceremony to begin. The popularity of this Games is extremely fervent. The tickets for each stadium, which began selling on the 15th, are disappearing rapidly. For the track and field stadium, swimming stadium, and other general seating areas, 80 to 90 percent had already been sold by 5 PM on the 20th. Four hundred thousand upper-class tickets for all competition days will be sold out entirely before the opening. The issue of economic contraction and unemployment is completely forgotten at this point, creating a sense of another world entirely. The number of people coming to Tokyo from the countryside to see the Games is increasing daily, and accommodations everywhere are overcrowded. Small retailers are mostly all smiles, and the thirty amusement venues around the grassy areas are all open. Merchants selling paintings and postcards of the Games have already appeared in the streets. The atmosphere of the Games permeates the entire city, it is said.

Japanese and Philippine Athletes Practicing

Tokyo, 21st - A telegram from the Associated Press reports that the Far Eastern Games are drawing nearer by the day. Before the afterglow of the Tokyo Six Universities League games has cooled, the Far Eastern Games are about to be presented. One hundred and nineteen Chinese athletes and one hundred and thirty-seven Philippine athletes are practicing vigorously every day. The Japanese athletes, who were decided on the 18th, also began formal practice at the youth association hostel from the 19th. The atmosphere of battle is gradually thickening in the Outer Garden of Meiji Shrine. The atmosphere of the Far Eastern Games is overflowing from the Outer Garden.

High Jump

Chronicle of the Voyage East by the Chinese Athlete Delegation (I)

(Jointly Recorded by Dong Shouyi, Wang Xiliang, and Sun Sijing on the Taiyo Maru)

Zhang Boling Convenes a Meeting with Instructions and Encouragement

Zhang Lingjia as the Chief Captain of the Athlete Delegation

The 9th Far Eastern Games, scheduled to be held in Tokyo, Japan, on the 24th of this month, will see the participation of over 130 Chinese athletes and staff members. They departed on the morning of the 15th, fully equipped, aboard the Taiyo Maru, sailing east. The details were recorded in a previous report. Now, having learned about the events and living conditions of the athlete delegation and staff members during the past two days on board, we will briefly describe them to inform those concerned about sports.

After boarding the ship, each athlete sought their own cabin and room, dividing into their respective quarters. Some shared rooms with two people, while others shared with four, all according to the pre-assigned rooms. Female athletes were assigned to first-class cabins, while male athletes were assigned to second-class cabins. Although the cabins were divided by class, the cleanliness of the ship's facilities and the thoughtfulness of its arrangement are said to make it one of the best ships on the Pacific route. The Chinese athletes felt comfortable in their daily routines and movements. Furthermore, the instructors were devoted and caring, so all the athletes were able to feel mentally satisfied and physically comfortable. This is truly what Dr. Zhang Boling meant when he said that the personality and spirit of the athletes are of utmost importance. Athlete meals are scheduled in the dining hall, with breakfast at 9 AM, lunch at 1 PM, and dinner at 7 PM each day. The teams eat together, side by side at the same table, in order to connect with each other and cultivate their character. The staff seats are located in the center of the hall, so all the athletes in the hall can clearly see any announcements. For athlete entertainment, outdoor activities are available during the day, and the deck is equipped with a swimming pool, table tennis, and various games. In the evenings, movies are screened in the main lounge. With comfort in dining and accommodation, coupled with adequate entertainment, the athletes' mental and physical well-being will undoubtedly be enhanced immensely. The details of each day on the ship will be recorded separately below.

May 15th

After the athletes boarded the ship, they went to find their places, with women staying in first class, men in second class, and staff elsewhere. Once everything was settled, they gathered in groups of three or five, strolling on the deck. Some gazed into the distance, some played games, and some chatted and laughed with each other. People from all over the north, south, east, and west, as well as overseas Chinese and women, were gathered on one ship. Their postures and attire varied greatly. Those from the north were upright and strong, those from the east were taller, those from the south were heroic and lively, and those from the Yangtze River area were graceful and agile. It was enough to represent the customs and habits of various places. Therefore, the deck scene was colorful and full of fun. At lunchtime, they entered in a line, each team joining together. The staff seats were located in the center of the hall. It was a happy gathering. After the meal, at about 2 PM, Hao Boyang convened a meeting of the entire Chinese athlete delegation and introduced Dr. Zhang Boling to speak about the mission of this trip and Hao Boyang's report. Then, each leader reported on the affairs of their respective teams, and they dispersed happily at 5 PM. Some athletes returned to their rooms to rest, while others exercised and played games. At this time, the Chinese basketball team, led by coach Dong Shouyi, performed basketball-style exercises on the deck for half an hour. These ten strong men were drenched in sweat.

At 7 PM, dinner was served. During the meal, the wind was gentle, but then it picked up, and the huge ship seemed uneasy. The ship's body shook quite a bit, and the northern athletes looked like they were about to throw up, so they rushed back to their rooms to lie down. Overseas Chinese and those from southern China ate and drank greedily, eating a hearty meal, as if nothing was happening. The joy of those who didn't get seasick was evident. At 10 PM, everyone returned to their rooms to sleep, and thus the daily life at sea came to an end.

Minutes of the Chinese Athlete Delegation Meeting

At 2 PM on May 15th, the Chinese athlete delegation held a plenary meeting in the second-class dining room of the Taiyo Maru. Chairman Hao Boyang, representative Zhang Boling spoke, saying that although the underdevelopment of Chinese sports has been affected by the political situation, there has been good progress in Chinese sports in the three years since the 8th Far Eastern Games. China has not yet been unified in terms of the political situation, but today in the sports field, athletes from the east, west, north, men and women can gather together to form a whole team, representing our country to attend the Far Eastern Games. This is enough to show that the people of our country are originally unified, without distinction between each other, and it can also let foreigners know that the reason why our country is not unified is only political. In the past few Far Eastern Games, we relied heavily on Westerners. Since the 8th Games, we have been fully responsible by ourselves. Especially this time, we are traveling eastward with such a full spirit, which shows the optimism of our country's sports future. The goal of the Far Eastern Games is not in winning or losing. Winning is certainly gratifying, but losing is also honorable. It is only up to us to work hard to express the purpose of sports. Leaders and athletes must know that the overall spirit is particularly good this time, which can represent that we have won half of the real victory in this Far Eastern Games. Furthermore, this trip to Japan, all measures should show the spirit of our great nation. In previous years, China and Japan both learned from the West as students, but Japan's progress is so rapid that it can almost be our teacher, so we should be more self-motivated and must try our best to make progress. If there are any points of dissatisfaction with the Games, if you want to file a protest, do not act alone or withdraw from a certain competition, or have any irregular behavior. We must protest according to the procedures. Our entire team must have the spirit of doing our best to support the success of the Games, and we must not have a prejudice to destroy it. In short, to achieve the above goals, first, each of us must take responsibility, not just rely on a few leaders. Second, we must obey the training of the instructors. Then, Chairman Hao Boyang reported: (1) Athletes must wear their badges and write their names on them so that they can get to know each other. (2) All athletes are not allowed to visit the B-deck. (3) Each team should set its own time for training on the ship every day. (4) Be sure to dress neatly during meals. Finally, the entire team elected two male flag bearers, Li Guochen and Lu Ming, and two female athletes, and elected Zhang Lingjia as the chief captain of the athlete delegation.

(China) Li Zhongsan

(Japan) Kimura Ono, Murayama, Takeda, Oda

(Philippines) Deli Biao, Lasuo, Suchenfa

(India) Yun Sasi

Long Jump

(China) Zhao Rugong, Wang Jihuai, Hao Chunde

The Chinese Team

The Grand Occasion in Kobe

(Correspondence from Yuan Weicun in Kobe)

Overseas Chinese Welcome at the Chinese Association

Zhang Boling Responds with a Sincere Thank You

The Athletes Take the Train to Tokyo That Night

Our country's athlete representatives participating in this year's Far Eastern Games, together with various staff members, totaled 167 people, led by Hao Boyang and Zhang Boling. They sailed east from Shanghai on the Taiyo Maru on the 15th of this month. At 4 PM on the 17th of this month, the ship arrived in Kobe. Those who went to the pier to greet them included various groups in Kobe and numerous students from Tongwen and Huaqiang, totaling about 3,000 people. As soon as the ship docked, the school students played music and sang the national anthem, waving the national flag. The athletes also raised their hats in return. Afterwards, they disembarked one after another, full of energy. Newspaper reporters took pictures one after another. They then boarded more than 30 cars prepared by the Chinese Association and drove in succession to the Association, where a welcoming tea party was held. The Vice Consul of Kobe, Ren Jiafeng, delivered a welcoming speech, followed by a response from Zhang Boling, who said, "Today, upon arriving in Japan, we have received a warm welcome from all of you fellow overseas Chinese, for which we are sincerely grateful. The Far Eastern Games have been held nine times so far, three times in the Philippines and three times in Japan. Each time our team has gone abroad, we have never had a more abundant spirit than this time. Therefore, we can be confident that the results this time will definitely be better than before. Our participation in the Games is not for a few trophies and a few silver cups. Winning or losing is irrelevant. We are only expressing our spirit of unity, because now foreigners don't know that our country has been divided into several countries. Look at the athletes who have come this time from as far north as Harbin and as far south as Hong Kong, as well as from distant Nanyang and Honolulu. There is no distinction between north and south. The spirit of unity is extremely strong. We are grateful to all of you for donating to the travel expenses. Now, on behalf of all the athletes, I would like to express my gratitude." Afterwards, the event was dismissed. The Kobe Chinese Boy Scouts led the way to the Central Pavilion for dinner. That night, they took the express train at 8:23 PM to Tokyo and arrived the next day, lodging at the Kanda Youth Hall.

Important News

Regulations for Registration of Chinese Boy Scouts

The Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts promulgated the Regulations for Registration of Chinese Boy Scouts on May 17, as follows:

Article 1: All Chinese children at home and abroad who are 12 years old or older, willing to receive Chinese Boy Scout training, and have the permission of their parents, must register with the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts in accordance with these Regulations. Article 2: Applicants must obtain a registration form from their respective troop headquarters, fill it out in detail, and submit it to the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts for review, along with a registration fee of three silver dollars. Article 3: In areas where there are no Boy Scout troops, applicants may submit a registration form directly to the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts with a certificate from their parents or a Chinese Boy Scout service member. Article 4: Applicants who pass the review by the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts will be issued a Chinese Boy Scout certificate and badge. Article 5: After the establishment of the Boy Scout Council in each locality, the registration matters in Articles 2 and 3 must be submitted by the Boy Scout Council at each locality, level by level, to the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts for review. Article 6: The Chinese Boy Scouts must hold registration once a year. Article 7: If there are any matters not covered in these Regulations, they shall be amended by the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts. Article 8: These Regulations shall be promulgated and implemented by the Headquarters of the Chinese Boy Scouts.

Statistics on Education Expenses in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province Over the Years

A Threefold Increase Compared to Previous Years

The actual educational expenses spent by various counties in Jiangsu Province within the four-year compulsory education stage of primary schools and primary school junior departments from the first year of the Republic of China to the seventeenth year of the Republic of China have been compiled by the Jiangsu Provincial Preparatory Office for Compulsory Education. A statistical table of primary school expenses in Jiangsu counties over the years has been prepared after multi-faceted investigations. The increase or decrease is compared separately according to the year and county. Since the Republic of China, the rise and fall of the educational expenses in Jiangsu Province can be clearly understood. The total amount of actual expenses for each year (61 counties in Jiangsu) is recorded below:

Year 1: 1,389,894 yuan

Year 2: 1,552,538 yuan

Year 3: 1,596,921 yuan

Year 4: 1,704,129 yuan

Year 5: 1,910,744 yuan

Year 6: 1,960,784 yuan

Year 7: 2,035,057 yuan

Year 8: 2,202,734 yuan

Year 9: 2,396,610 yuan

Year 10: 2,504,999 yuan

Year 11: 2,619,958 yuan

Year 12: 2,710,875 yuan

Year 13: 2,776,699 yuan

Year 14: 2,851,435 yuan

Year 15: 2,605,954 yuan

Year 16: 3,291,284 yuan

Year 17: 4,198,498 yuan

According to the above statistics, Year 17 increased by 2,808,604 yuan compared to Year 1, a threefold increase. However, the expenses for Year 15 decreased by 245,481 yuan compared to the previous year, likely due to the disruption of schools in various counties during the early stages of the revolution in Jiangsu, leading to the diversion of funds. This shows that the education sector is closely related to local security. After Year 17, with the gradual arrival of the Tutelage Period, compulsory education gained increasing importance.

市宣傅部指導科議定

Measures for Preventing Cultural Aggression

The Guidance Section of the Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipality Executive Committee held its fifth section meeting yesterday (the 20th) at 2:00 PM. The meeting was chaired by Xu Xingchu, with Zhou Hanmei as the recorder. The following items were discussed: (1) The request to approve the central government's plan to expand propaganda based on the key points of propaganda for this week was approved; (2) The measures for commemorating the May 30th Massacre, already drafted, were approved; (3) The measures for commemorating the anniversary of Premier Sun Yat-sen's interment on June 1st, already drafted, were approved, and it was resolved to submit them to the minister for submission to the Municipal Executive Committee; (4) The measures for preventing imperialist cultural aggression, already drafted, were approved, and it was resolved to submit them to the minister for submission to the Municipal Executive Committee. The meeting was adjourned. Appended below are the measures for preventing imperialist cultural aggression passed by the section: 1. Non-citizens of the Republic of China or organizations not entirely composed of citizens of the Republic of China shall not be allowed to establish primary schools, kindergartens, or normal schools for educating Chinese people. All teachers and staff in primary schools or kindergartens shall be limited to citizens of the Republic of China. 2. Starting from the 19th year of the Republic (1930), graduates of church schools that have not been approved and registered by Chinese authorities shall not receive the same treatment as graduates of registered schools. Church schools that offer religious subjects or hold religious ceremonies on campus shall not be allowed to register. Church schools that have been rejected for registration or have failed to apply for registration by the deadline shall be ordered to close within a set time limit. 3. All church schools applying for registration shall be thoroughly investigated by the Education Department or the Municipal/County Education Bureau. After the application is forwarded and approved for registration, the original investigating agency shall be responsible for regularly examining whether there are any instances of privately conducting religious propaganda. If any violations of the regulations are found, they shall be immediately dealt with. For all church schools that have been approved for registration, the principal shall be directly appointed by the competent Chinese authorities, but the school's board of directors shall have the power of supervision. If the principal is deemed incompetent, the board of directors shall be allowed to submit a request to the competent Chinese authorities to investigate and appoint another person. 4. No religious organizations shall use the names of preaching halls or theological seminaries to gather Chinese children to teach them religious subjects. Organizations that are actually engaged in religious research shall not be allowed to have underage citizens of the Republic of China participate. Violators shall be immediately shut down. 5. Although the YMCA in the country ostensibly promotes moral, intellectual, physical, and social development, in reality, it propagates Christianity, seducing young people and is clearly an instrument of imperialist cultural aggression. Chinese educational institutions should take over and manage them independently. 6. All organizations with religious characteristics must be handled in accordance with the organizational plan for people's groups promulgated by the Central Committee of the Party. Publications of all church schools or organizations shall be submitted to the local highest party headquarters for review on a regular basis. 7. If foreigners, under the pretext of cultural investigation, go to various parts of China and develop antiquities without authorization, all items shall be confiscated and they shall be deported.

Free Talk

A Laughing Matter · Hai · Ke

Wife: Why do you always just listen to the radio and not like listening to me?

Husband: Because it always has good music and good songs that please my ears, and it never scolds or blames me.

Girl A: I'm getting married soon.

Girl B: How come I don't know anything about it?

Girl A: Because my lover and I advocate a secret marriage, we agreed not to let anyone know and solemnly swore that whoever tells will be less than human.

A: I don't understand how you have so much money to take your girlfriend out to restaurants all the time.

B: It's a secret. I only pick girlfriends who are gaining weight to go with me. They're so afraid of getting fatter that they don't dare eat much, so I don't have to spend too much.

A: No one in your family trusts doctors. What happens if you get a really bad illness?

B: We can die freely and avoid being force-fed medicine and undergoing the misery of surgery.

Girl A: My fiancé has given me his whole heart.

Girl B: You should be careful. He sent his heart to me last time. I cherished it so much, but he complained that I broke his heart.

A Startling Glimpse · Wu · Mo · Xi

On the 18th, I visited the 30th-anniversary celebration at the Toa Dobun Shoin College at the invitation of a friend. I arrived at the college at 2:00 PM. Guests were given a well-made commemorative booklet. We first went to the music room to listen to music. In addition to famous Western pieces, there was a harmonica ensemble, which was quite wonderful. Finally, there was a shamisen ensemble by the "Miyako no Haru Koto Tomo no Kai." Two men played the "shakuhachi," which looks like a flute but is thicker, and its sound is very clear. Five women played stringed instruments that resemble the Chinese zither. I heard that each instrument costs 300 yuan. They sang while playing, and the sound was harmonious, somewhat like Sanskrit chanting, both mournful and moving. It lasted a long time before it ended. After that, we visited the "ryosai" (寮祭). "Ryosai" refers to the free arrangement of each classroom. Everywhere there was deep meaning, and mostly they were critiques of current events in China and Japan, such as the austerity policies in Japan and the political struggles between Chiang Kai-shek and Yan Xishan in China. Among them, what I appreciated most was the surface and the interior of the Four Horse Road. On the surface, there were publications from various bookstores, seemingly to improve culture, but inside were sex histories, spring books, and prostitutes, all of which lead people to depravity. It is impossible not to nod in agreement after seeing this. Another was the love suicide incident of the Japanese writer Takeo Arishima. The room was decorated with a grave door and weeds, all in a mournful green, with a cold wind whistling. Two skeletons were kissing among the reeds, and the title was "Kiss of the Spirits." It was truly a work full of artistic meaning. Others, such as a room with only one hole left, and looking inside revealed only darkness, with the words "The Current State of China" written in large letters outside the room, the meaning was clear and thought-provoking. After the viewing, we visited the library again. I entered the research room. All kinds of magazines from China and abroad were available, but I paid particular attention to the research on China. There was a bookshelf with dozens of volumes of elaborately bound books, and there were five or six books specifically studying the content of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang War. It was astonishing to see this. Another room displayed photographs of the situation in the Chinese interior, as detailed as the scenery of Guizhou and the upper reaches of the Ou River in Zhejiang, and as detailed as the ancient sites near Xi'an, all of which are not easily seen by us, and many of them have artistic value. But what was most startling was the printed matter of the May 15 Incident. Such as the manifestos of May 15, May 17, and May 19, and the slogans of the May 30th, all of which were collected in detail and compiled into volumes. As for the various declarations of the National Government, they were all mounted like album pages. Various anti-communist and anti-Chiang propaganda materials were classified and filed. From this, it can be seen that the Japanese have been planning for a long time and value research over lip service, which is far beyond what the people of the old great powers can hope to achieve. I heard from a friend that the school's operating expenses are 3 million yuan per year, all paid by the Japanese government. Even Central University and Jiaotong University in China only have 2 million yuan per year. Each month, students are sent to China for inspection, while Chinese students are sent to Japan. When they go, Japanese people greet them everywhere, and they are entertained every day. Therefore, what they get is only superficial, and they only enjoy a taste of material pleasure. On the lawn inside the school gate, there is a newly erected bronze statue of the former president, Nezu. This person was the most vocal advocate for the establishment of the Toa Dobun Shoin College and was also a schemer for invading China. This time, three of the Japanese Cabinet Ministers specifically sent people to China to give instructions. One of them was an elderly duke. It's just a small school, but it is valued so much. The reason for this is worth pondering deeply. I felt uneasy after returning, so I wrote this messily to tell my countrymen.

A Record of the Bronze Drum of Zhuge in Jinshan · Tao · An

In a certain Brahma house of Jiangtian Temple in Zhenjiang, there is a bronze drum of Zhuge Liang, which he used to boost the morale of soldiers when he assisted the Shu Han. It is similar in size to ordinary ones, made of firm and heavy material, and dark in color. When struck, it rings clearly like a chime stone. The casting and painting are extremely refined. The pattern engraved on the face resembles the planets orbiting the sun, with twelve corners, just like the party emblem. This is purely a coincidence and nothing to be surprised about. After the revolutionary army settled in Jingjiang, the flag of the Blue Sky with a White Sun was raised all over the north and south of the Yangtze River. The monks of the temple thought it resembled the painting on the drum surface and regarded it as mysterious. They used it to solicit money from people. From then on, visitors from all directions scrambled to view and donate. This bronze drum of Zhuge, which had been unknown for thousands of years, became famous after this propaganda. In the future, it will be immortalized with the Ling Mountain Pagoda.

A Record of an Industrialist in Pudong Awakening · Tao · An

Ling Xiufeng of Qituan, Nanhui, is the owner of the Jinlun Towel Factory. Today, among domestic towels, the products of the Sanyou Industrial Society and the Jinlun Towel Factory are the best. The Jinlun Towel Factory was founded after May 9, 1915. At that time, Ling was stimulated by Japan and believed that only by revitalizing industry could the national humiliation be avenged, and only by promoting domestic goods could the motherland be saved. However, although Ling had this ambition, he did not have much capital. He set up a towel factory in his hometown, named Jinlun, with twenty machines. On the one hand, he hired rural women to weave towels, and on the other hand, he led his wife and children to bleach, dry, and decorate them. Therefore, although he was a factory owner, he was barefoot and disheveled all day long, personally doing menial labor. People only thought he was a worker in the factory and did not know he was the owner of the factory. After the goods were made, he took them to Shanghai to sell them to merchants. When he sold them, he wore a coarse cloth and trudged through the market. People thought he was a salesman and did not know he was the owner of the factory. At that time, the merchants in Shanghai, because his brand was not well-known and his sales were not widespread, deliberately made trouble and suppressed him. Ling lowered his head and humbly improved the goods that needed to be improved. He made efforts to lower the prices that could be lowered, so that the merchants had no excuse. Therefore, his costs were higher than others, and his profits were lower than others. As a result, in just a few years, the products of the Jinlun Factory gained people's trust and sales greatly increased. Therefore, since the factory was established fifteen years ago, the number of machines and the number of employees have increased every year. Today, the factory has as many as 800 machines and employs thousands of workers. It is really different from when it was first established. Today, its towels are sold not only in various provinces but also in various parts of the world. Today, the Chinese people use domestic towels, making foreign goods disappear. Ling has made a great contribution to this. Therefore, Ling can be said to be a successful entrepreneur. However, in the early days of its establishment, he was willing to do menial labor when shipping goods and was willing to endure people's arrogance when selling them. Only because of his perseverance did he have today's success. I record this to tell the entrepreneurs of today's revitalization industry.

English and American Jottings · Li · Shu · Ping

Red Carpet

Seven Star Lamp, Xu Xiaoting

The other night, I saw the 90-year-old Sun Juxian perform the Seven Star Lamp on the Shanghai stage. This play starts with the burning of the Calabash Valley. Old Ju's Kongming was supported by two pageboys when he came on stage. His steps were quite steady. He was not slowed down by wearing a net cap and thick-soled boots. He is truly a person of longevity. The order of sending generals was well-organized. His singing was also well-tuned, which proves that his memory and hearing are still strong. The second time he came on stage, he heard Ma Dai report that the landmines buried in the Calabash Valley had been destroyed by the heavy rain, and Sima Yi and his son and Wei Yan had all escaped. However, he suddenly stood up from his seat, and a look of anxiety appeared on his face at the same time. Then he sat back down. This expression is most suitable for the quiet Kongming. It is much more appropriate than the usual shouting of "Aww." After sitting down, he did not make useless complaints. He immediately said, "If Wei Yan comes back, there will be a quarrel." This point is where Kongming's knowledge of what is urgent surpasses others. Therefore, he falsely accused Ma Dai to appease Wei Yan's anger. Old Ju showed Kongming's alertness in feigning anger and smiling falsely. Everyone in the audience nodded and smiled. When the flag bearer delivered the order, Kongming asked about the reason for the flag bearer's mistake in revealing the truth that he ate little and was busy with many things, which was due to his greed for Sima Yi's banquet. He became anxious, his beard trembled, and he angrily pointed at the flag bearer with his feather fan. The flag bearer retreated from the left side of the seat to the right side, forming an arc. The feather fan also followed from left to right. This is extremely vivid. This old man is truly not old. The "Looking Up to the Sky" segment of the Erhuang Yuanban has a pure and rich flavor. The ceremony of worshiping the lamp was first escorted by the manager of the stage, Chang Yunheng, and the famous amateur singer, Mr. Chen Gangshu. Old Ju suddenly broke away from the two and walked alone to the Nine Dragon Mouth, singing the slow Erhuang segment "Sighing for Emperor Gao." How strong he is! This segment has not been shortened. The "Xing" character in "Guangwu Xing" and the "Ya" character in "Ba Zhu Qiya" were dragged out with long tunes, and the charm was as vast as in the past. The words of the prayer for expelling stars were elegant and sincere. Tan Xinpei would never have this talent. The "Ji" character in "Huang Tian Hou Tu He Qi Si Ji" used three trembling tones to conclude. The sound was unusually loud and full of emotion. This is Old Ju's unique skill. The "Zhuge Liang Ye Fei Shi" segment of the Yuanban was a wonderful expression of the essence of the performance. The Erhuang Yaoban, which was on the verge of death, used high notes in two places, and the capture and release were appropriate. Listening to it was like taking a dose of Qingxin powder. When singing the "Shi" character in "Wuchang Dao Wan Shi Xiu," he repeatedly trembled his head as if spitting blood. The lingering sound also trembled. It was truly very tragic. Just these few sentences of singing and a few expressions are enough to surpass a whole play of a mediocre young sheng (an actor who plays young male roles). Mr. Chen Gangshu, Old Ju's proud disciple, recorded the above three major Erhuang segments of this play at the Great China Record Company the year before last. It has Old Ju's charm. Since the old man did not leave any real records, Gangshu's film is especially precious. It is the absolute best of the Fu Sun school. (Gratitude)

It is very popular in London to keep ponies. They weigh less than eighty pounds, and their fur is of various colors, all of which are bright and dazzling. They are docile and lively, very comparable to horses. Most fashionable young women treat them like pet dogs and always take them out for walks. These horses come from the Shetland Islands in the west and are quite expensive. The United States has also recently purchased a large number of them for children to drive, but they did not adapt to the climate and many of them died.

British Labour MP Ms. Eleanor Rathbone has recently proposed repealing the Women's Nationality Act of 1870 and creating a new law that "any British woman who marries a foreigner should still retain her British nationality, unless she voluntarily takes the nationality of her husband." It has now been passed by Parliament and promulgated for implementation.

British women have recently liked to wear monocles. Those who advocate it most strongly include Labour MP Ms. Eleanor Rathbone, the famous novelist Ms. Joan, and many artists and educators. Once this trend started, American women immediately followed suit.

The number of divorce cases in the United States has been increasing very rapidly in recent years. The government has no way to stop it. According to the new statistics for 1929, the number of divorces has increased from 195,939 to 214,495. The increase rate in most provinces is 74%. If the ratio of marriage to divorce is compared, it is 6 to 1.

The Chicago School of Aesthetic Makeup claims that American women will tend to have yellow skin this summer. After bathing in the sea, they will also take sunbaths to burn their skin and turn it yellow. In this way, the vermilion color between the lips must also be thickened at the same time. The harmony of the two colors will complement each other. They are now re-manufacturing lip gloss to make it fragrant and greasy. It is estimated that the sales of this lip gloss will be more than 200 million.

Warmth in the Heart (1)(9)(7) · Bao · Tian · Xiao

Chapter Eleven: Emerald Network and Pearl Hairpins: A Fair Lady Returns to a Fine Gentleman's Green House and Red Tent, and a Famous Courtesan Marries a Renowned Man

However, Liu Xing Shu had already accepted the translation work. This was like a fixed order in the business world, and the goods had to be delivered on time. He had no choice but to rush to finish it day and night. Fortunately, his writing was always very quick, and he was good at foreign languages. Translating novels is not like translating scientific books, which have all kinds of scientific terms that need to be revised. Translating novels only requires the writing to be fluent and smooth, especially detective novels, which must be consistent from beginning to end and not contradict each other. Indeed, every day he went back, from ten o'clock to one o'clock, he could translate a lot of words. And sometimes when he was happy, or when a section of events in the translation, it had to be translated in one go, he would not put down his pen until he heard the one o'clock chime. Then he would lose his interest. Sometimes his midnight work went to two or three o'clock before he went to sleep. Although Liu Xing Shu boasted that he only slept six hours every night, he was still young. Sleeping eight hours was not too much. Therefore, he did more work and felt that he was not getting enough sleep and had no time to rest and play. A person is like a machine, running day and night, and the machine will feel tired. Moreover, Liu Xing Shu's body was not very healthy to begin with. Therefore, he gradually developed symptoms of illness. One day, he said to Zuo Shi Chen, "You say that a person needs to sleep an average of eight hours every night, but now I can't believe your words more and more. For example, if I translate more books at night and go to sleep at three o'clock, sometimes I can't fall asleep when I get into bed. Occasionally, I doze off, but when it gets light, I always wake up. Or if I go to bed an hour earlier, I wake up in the middle of the night and look at the sky with wide eyes, feeling very uncomfortable. According to this calculation, I never get eight hours of sleep every day." In fact, he had already contracted insomnia. Because he liked to think hard and change his mind. Whenever a person can't fall asleep, they start to think randomly. The more they want to sleep, the less they can sleep. The more they can't sleep, the more they think. Because they do too much work and are too busy, they get all fired up. So at night, their faces often turn red, and their cheeks are slightly red. They also gradually cough. One day, Zuo Shi Chen went to see him at his Ming Bao newspaper office. The Ming Bao newspaper office was in a room in the Ming Zhong Club. Their editorial department was just one big room, where everyone worked. Zuo Shi Chen often went to their editorial department. He knew several reporters. Zuo Shi Chen sat at Liu Yin Shu's desk. He was translating Western newspapers while talking to Zuo Shi Chen. But he heard his newly started cough. In one minute, he would cough two or three times, or even four or five times. Zuo Shi Chen felt that this cough did not sound good.

Gold Market: Latent Signs of Weakness

Reaction After Three Days of Continuous Rise

Changeable and without any standard, yesterday's gold market conditions remained confusing and erratic, with drastic fluctuations that made people feel frenzied, drunk, and foolish, unable to grasp anything. Prices still rose and fell by several taels at a time. However, a downward trend was lurking. The morning market saw a difference of more than seven taels, while the afternoon market was relatively stable, fluctuating by only one and a half taels. The foreign exchange market remained stable. Trading among dealers was not active. Companies like Wanxing, Yu Tai, Fuxing Yong, and Yuanmao Yong were mostly selling, while Fuchang, Yuancheng Yong, and Hengxing were entering and exiting intermittently. Since the morning market was filled with rumors that a silver tax was about to be implemented, causing fear among the general public, a storm arose, and the market opened low. Soon after, it rose sharply, fluctuating by more than four taels. Subsequently, Yu Tai, Fuxing Yong, and others sold aggressively, causing a sharp drop of six or seven taels from over 521 taels to 514 taels. In an instant, all parties seized the opportunity to purchase, resulting in a surge of five or six taels, followed by a slight correction of two or three taels. The market was in an indescribable state of chaos. Later, Wanxing, Shunli, Hengxing, and others sold slightly, and there were very few buyers. However, the market sentiment was uncertain, with fluctuations of just over one tael. The foreign exchange market was inactive.

The market opened with a decline, fluctuating by more than seven taels. The price of British silver rebounded by one-sixteenth, while the price of American silver still fell by three-eighths. The price of gold for July opened at 518 taels and 5 qian, immediately falling by 2 taels and 4 qian. Gross margins fluctuated by more than four taels. Initially, it was 17 taels, then it reached 21 taels and a half. When the first order was announced, it was 18 taels and a half, and the listed price remained unchanged. However, for July, the British gold wheat traders bought at 9 pence and 9375. For June, banks traded among themselves at 9 pence and 875. Subsequently, retail investors bought, pushing the price as high as 20 taels and 02 qian. Then, large investors sold off, and with British gold firming, the wheat trading company bought July at 10 pence and 125, causing a sharp drop of 6 taels to 10.0, to 14 taels. Suddenly, due to hedging by various firms and short sellers entering the market, and with various exchange rates firming, there was a jump of over five or six taels. After 11 o'clock, it was 20 taels. However, sellers remained persistent, and the price has now fallen back by 3 taels. At noon, the closing price was 17 taels and 7 qian.

The afternoon market was slightly calmer, resulting in a small drop of 2 taels and 4 qian. The afternoon market opened at 18 taels, then rose from 17 taels and 5 qian to 18 taels and 8 qian. In an instant, it fell back to 17 taels and 3 qian. After 2:30, there were fluctuations of one tael. Subsequently, due to more buyers, it rebounded to 18 taels and 8 qian. After 3:30, it turned downward again, falling slightly by one tael. At 4 o'clock, it was 17 taels and a half, truly a situation where selling led to a slight decline. However, various exchange rates happened to be inactive on Wednesday. Finally, some retail short sellers covered their positions, so the closing price at 4:30 was 518 taels and a half, a drop of more than 2 taels compared to the previous day, a reversal after three days of consecutive gains.

The daily exchange rate announcement was down 23 taels. The highest price of the day was 21 taels and 5 qian, and the lowest price was 14 taels, a difference of 7 taels and 5 qian. The announced price was still 541 taels and 8 qian, a decrease of 23 or 24 taels. The afternoon price was still suppressed at over 23 taels for accounting purposes, with a premium of 18 taels in the morning and 19 taels in the afternoon. Goods opened at 19 taels in the morning and closed at 18 taels in the afternoon, with the afternoon closing price at 17 taels and a half and 19 taels.
