Yili New Cocoons Have a Poor Harvest

With only 40% of the normal yield, cocoon merchants open their scales sparsely.

Yixing and Liyang are both cocoon-producing areas. Recently, they have been affected by banditry, and silkworm farming has declined. This year, the atmosphere of banditry is still rampant, and farmers dare not raise many silkworm eggs. In addition, the climate is out of sync, with cold weather and heavy rain, causing great damage to silkworm ants. Currently, in both Yixing and Liyang, early silkworms have already spun their cocoons, and late silkworms are just starting to emerge. Those who ask about going to the silkworm frames are present. The other day, it rained all day, and from hot to cold, the silkworm moths changed again, and the sleep heads did not rise. This year, the cocoon production in the four rural areas is bound to be poor. The address is at most 40% of the normal years. The cocoon merchants in each village are afraid of banditry, and those who open their scales are as few as the agricultural stars. Only the urban areas and market towns near the city still have exchange coupons to open their scales. Statistics are less than two or three-tenths of past years, it is said.

Cocoon Prices in Hangzhou Soar

The prices of improved varieties of high-quality cocoons have already opened above 80 yuan.

Cocoon merchants in Linping, Tangxi Pingyao, Gongchen Bridge, Gengshanmen, and other places in Hangzhou have been opening their scales for over a week. The market arrival is quite prosperous. Each line actively competes to collect cocoons. Cocoon prices have risen from 55 or 56 yuan to 67 or 68 yuan. The other day, it was cloudy and rainy all day, and the arrival was sparse. Each cocoon line is afraid that this year's Zhejiang cocoon production will have to discount 20% off from last year. They are deeply afraid that raw materials will panic in the future, and they all hold a multi-collection principle and release prices to compete for collection. Yesterday, the sky cleared slightly from the rain, and the arrival still did not appear crowded. Cocoon prices soared. Improved varieties of high-quality goods prices have already risen to more than 80 yuan, it is said.

Qicha Opens to 220 Taels

Since Qimen black tea was launched on the market on Sunday, the British tea houses have spared no effort in searching for goods with excellent leaf bottom production methods. However, the supply of this high-quality tea is in short supply, and the market price has already picked up to 220 taels, opening a new record unprecedented. However, the British houses' interest in Qining black teas from various medium and low-quality farms is still weak, because the London market has a large stock of Indian tea, which is difficult to compete with. As for the green tea market, the sales of native farm Zhenmei have completely stopped, and the products from Suian are also not considered to be a good image, it is said.

Flour: Long Positions Sold, Afternoon Returns Weak

Yesterday, the flour market presented a picture of first firmness, then weakness. At the initial opening of the morning, with the unceasing rain, people's hearts turned high, but in the subsequent sessions, many long positions, near and far term, issued from the outside. After the festival rise, the general inland help was in a state of glee, as if they had an unthinkable feeling, so they seized this opportunity and were unwilling to get involved again, selling at any time. Originally, the formation of this situation was caused by the squeeze, and the inland help's looting also gained a lot of assistance. Observing the subsequent steps, with the factory still in a non-relaxed state, too much relaxation will have to wait until the new wheat season. The result was that the current month was a little 5 li less than the previous day, June was a little 2.5 li, July and August did not move, September was a little 5 li, and October did not move, it was said.

Wheat Market: Futures and Spot Did Not Rise or Fall

Yesterday, the wheat market largely presented a picture of circling. Foreign wheat was quoted at 457 jiao, but speculators could not help but have some concerns due to the cloudy and rainy weather. However, the harvest season of new wheat is still about two weeks away, so it is not yet urgent. However, the closer it is to the harvest season, the more it will be slightly affected. As a result, the June, July, and August months did not move, and the September and October months were slightly less one fen. Spot wheat trading was still scarce. The opening prices of each wharf were also seldom up or down. After this, the old wheat will reach its expiration, and the new goods can replace it, this kind of market can be difficult to be high again. The opening price for Xuzhou wheat, Bengbu wheat, and Shandong wheat was 5 taels, 1 qian, and 7 fen. The opening prices for Hankou wheat were 4 taels, 5 qian, and half and 4 taels, 4 qian, and 3 fen, for a total of 1,500 bales, it was said.

Foreign Rice Increased Again Due to Jiangxi Buying

Yesterday, the prices of foreign rice were still weak in the morning after the market opened due to ample arrivals and storage. In the afternoon, Jiangxi help and Zhejiang road suddenly searched for buying in the street, and the situation immediately turned around. All rice rose 5 or 6 points, and small sizes became more sought-after. The total market transaction was 6,000 bags of small sizes, priced at 14 yuan, 3 jiao, and half, and 2,000 bags of brown rice, priced at 13 yuan, 1 jiao, and 3 fen. 3,000 bags of large sizes, priced at 14 yuan and 1 jiao. 500 bags of No. 1 Saigon, priced at 15 yuan and 1 jiao, and 300 bags of No. 2, priced at 14 yuan and 4 jiao, it was said.

Seafood: The first season shrimp roe from Jiangbei arrived yesterday, with three loads.

Selling price: 180 to 195 taels

Shrimp and crab and fish, the old goods have long been out of stock. The new goods were harvested poorly due to the wrong season. Yesterday, the first season of shrimp roe from Jiangbei arrived, with 300 hundred jin, and was sold for 180 to 195 taels. The goods were wet, and the color was withered and black. As it was the first batch, key buyers were still stylish, and it was sold to the street and the Han help. It is said that the second batch of goods can also be delivered in a few days, and subsequent market prices are protected against turning down. New crabs have recently been shipped from Tianjin, Ningbo, and Jiangbei for sale. The original dry good goods were 75 taels, and the colored goods were 60 to 68 taels.

Hardware: Galvanized Iron: Galvanized Iron Tiles are Flourishing

Recently, galvanized iron, whether British or American goods, has shown a flourishing trend. Since the recent sharp contraction of foreign exchange, the cost of all goods has increased sharply, especially Japanese goods. The price of Japanese goods is more than 10% higher than in Shanghai, so the industry has not placed any orders. At present, the estimated price of British goods is 11 taels, 2 qian, and half per load for 24 gauge, 12 taels for 26 gauge, 12 taels and 7 qian and half for 28 gauge, and 13 taels and 8 qian and half for 31 gauge. For American goods, the estimated price is 12 taels and 2 qian and half for 24 gauge, 13 taels and 7 qian and half for 26 gauge, 14 taels and 7 qian and half for 28 gauge, and 14 taels for 48 gauge. Transactions with the Yangtze River and Fujian and Zhejiang groups are smoother, while business on the northern roads seems deserted, it was said.

Galvanized iron tiles: With the yellow plum season approaching, the northern roads have increased their purchases, so the market goods have been almost exhausted. The flow of standard goods is very scarce, resulting in a shortage of supply. Market prices are extraordinarily high, such as an estimated 10 taels and 5

National General Chamber of Commerce Appeals

Stop Throwing Bombs at Merchants and Civilians

The National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, the Red Cross Society, the Disaster Relief Committee, and the Shanghai Office, etc., recently received a telegram from the Henan Relief Committee, the Henan Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, and the Red Cross Branch, which read: "Our Henan people have suffered from natural disasters and banditry for years, and the people are living in misery, in dire straits. Recently, wars have broken out in Henan Province, and planes from various routes in the southeast have arrived one after another, throwing bombs. Areas such as Guide, Lanfeng, and Kaifeng in the east, as well as the area south of Zhengzhou, have suffered countless deaths and destruction of civilian houses. Whenever planes arrive, the old and young, men and women, are unable to defend themselves, and the cries shake the earth. The tragic situation is unbearable to witness. We believe that the authorities, as advanced members of the Party and the country, and with compassion for the people, will surely be moved by such a tragic disaster. Moreover, places like Kaifeng, Zhengzhou, and Lanfeng are not war zones. It is even more pitiful that our innocent people are made such meaningless sacrifices. Our association has received urgent requests from the people and has already telegraphed Commander-in-Chief Chiang and the Commanders-in-Chief of Xuzhou and Hankou to stop this, but we have not received a response. The people are even more frightened, so we telegraphed your esteemed association again, asking you to convey public opinion and request Commander-in-Chief Chiang to instruct the front lines to refrain from sending planes to Henan to throw bombs, in order to reassure the people and protect the lives of all. We will be eternally grateful. We also hope for a telegraphic reply. Respectfully, the Henan Relief Committee, the Henan Provincial Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Chinese and Foreign Relief Association, and the Red Cross Branch." After receiving the telegram, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce telegraphed Chairman Chiang yesterday, saying, "Respectfully presented to Commander-in-Chief Chiang of Xuzhou. We have received a telegram from the Henan Relief Committee, the Federation of Chambers of Commerce, the Relief Association, and the Red Cross Society, begging that planes refrain from throwing bombs at merchants and civilians in Henan Province. We are forwarding this telegram on their behalf. We hope that you will instruct all routes to comply. Respectfully, the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce."

Inspections to Begin Next Month

The Navy has decided to inspect fleets in various locations starting on the first of next month. Chen Xunyong, commander of the training fleet, will be responsible for the inspections in Shanghai and Hong Kong, but the dates have not yet been determined. Yesterday, the Chu Qian warship also arrived in Shanghai from Fujian for inspection. Waters off Lusi, Tongzhou

Occupied by Pirates

Fourth District of the Water Police Dispatches the Ce Dian and Ping Yang Warships

Seventeenth and Eighteenth Patrol Boat Teams to Conduct Suppression

In the waters off Lusi, Tongzhou, outside Wusongkou, more than twenty large pirate ships have been discovered in recent days, with six or seven hundred pirates on board. They are looting ships and colluding with local bandits on land, and are extremely rampant. This was reported in this newspaper on the 20th. Zhu Bingzheng, the district chief of the Fourth District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police in Wusong, received a report yesterday that the pirates and land bandits had already intercepted and occupied the coastal area near Lusi. Their power is even greater than before. The middle and upper-class families in the area have mostly moved away. After receiving the report, District Chief Zhu immediately ordered the captains of the Ce Dian and Ping Yang warships, Lu Gongren and Gong Mianqin, and the captains of the Seventeenth and Eighteenth Patrol Boat Teams, Chen Xin, to lead the Ce Dian and Ping Yang warships (with Captain Gong also serving as captain of the Ping Yang) and the Seventeenth and Eighteenth Patrol Boat Teams to set off from Songjiang at 1:00 PM yesterday and head to Lusi to conduct a suppression.

Du Yuesheng Mediates

French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Strike

Resumed Work After a Half-Hour Work Stoppage Yesterday Morning

The Shanghai French Concession Water and Electricity Workers' Union presented six demands to the company on May 19, with a deadline for a reply. Because the company's attitude was strong and it refused to acknowledge the demands, a temporary general meeting was held in the factory at 5:00 PM on the 20th. It was decided that work would be stopped on the morning of the 21st to awaken the company. Later, Du Yuesheng sent representatives to discuss the matter with Xu A’mei and others from the union, suggesting that it would be best to avoid a work stoppage in May. After discussion, the union agreed to Du's suggestion and temporarily resumed work. It is reported that the work stoppage lasted about half an hour.

Public Concession Tram Workers

Determined to Strike Today to Rescue Ten Arrested Fellow Workers

After announcing the resumption of work on the 17th of this month, the tram workers in the Public Concession were concerned about the ten fellow workers who had been arrested. The foremen conveyed the company's intention to release them this Thursday (the 22nd). Because the deadline has passed, the club specially convened all the workers yesterday and decided that all workers would hold a strike starting at 10:00 AM on Thursday (today) until the ten workers are released and reinstated. The company and the police are currently trying to resolve the situation.

Nine New Chinese Cotton Mills

Total Spindles: 120,000

According to a survey yesterday, Chinese cotton mills have been developing rapidly recently. There are nine new mills and branch mills that have recently been established or are in preparation. The planned number of spindles is approximately 120,000. There are several more whose plans have not yet been finalized. The list of factories is as follows: Shen Xin 囗, Shashi, Yong Yu, Pu Yi, Liao Ying, Yichang, Hua Chang, Ji Sheng, and Yi Feng.

Collection of

Regulations on Real Estate Transfer Tax

Announced by the Municipal Government Yesterday

The Municipal Government announced the Provisional Regulations for the Collection of Real Estate Transfer Tax in this city yesterday, which are as follows: "Now, the Provisional Regulations for the Collection of Real Estate Transfer Tax in the Shanghai Special Municipality are hereby formulated and promulgated. This order is hereby given." The text of the regulations is recorded as follows: Article 1: Anyone who mortgages or buys real estate within this Special Municipality shall, within three months from the date of establishing the contract, bring the contract and the mortgaged or purchased field deed or land certificate, as well as the original owner's grain string and transfer certificate, to the Land Bureau to pay the real estate transfer tax. Article 2: The real estate transfer tax in this Special Municipality is levied at a rate of four yuan per hundred yuan of the contract price for mortgage contracts and eight yuan per hundred yuan of the contract price for sales contracts. Article 3: After the people pay the transfer tax at the Land Bureau, they will be given a receipt with the seals of both the Finance and Land Bureaus. One week later, they can retrieve the contract with the receipt. Article 4: For those who pay the real estate transfer tax after the deadline, if it is less than three months late, the sales contract will be subject to an additional tax of four yuan per hundred yuan of the original tax amount; if it is more than three months but less than six months late, the additional tax will be eight yuan per hundred yuan; if it is more than six months but less than nine months late, the additional tax will be twelve yuan per hundred yuan. The additional tax for mortgage contracts will be reduced by half. If the payment is not made within one year from the date of establishing the contract, the Land Bureau will notify the Public Security Bureau by letter and send police officers to the bureau together with the local security officer to order the owner to pay. Article 5: If people mortgage or buy real estate and underreport the contract price in an attempt to reduce taxes, once it is verified, the underreported amount will be subject to twice the original tax rate. If the payment is made after the deadline, the additional tax will still be levied according to Article 4. Article 6: After people mortgage or buy real estate and pay the transfer tax, the Land Bureau will note the tax amount on the real estate contract, affix a seal, and return it to the owner. The registration and transfer will be completed with the transfer certificate. Article 7: These regulations shall be submitted by the Shanghai Special Municipal Government to the Ministry of Finance for record and implementation."

Rice and Grain

Recent Meeting of the Fair Price Committee

Organize a Fundraising Team to Solicit Donations

Suspend Rice Sales for Three Days During Account Closing

The Shanghai Municipal Rice and Grain Fair Price Committee held its fourth meeting at the Social Affairs Bureau at 2:00 PM on the 20th. The committee members present were Yao Zirang, Ye Huijun, Zhu Zixiang, Sun Yishan, Tang Naikang (represented by Chen Tian), Xu Fu (represented by Xu Fengzao), Huang Hanzhi, Wang Boxun, Yan Xiaoquan, Fan Hesheng, Lu Wenshao, Yuan Liang (represented by Zhao Zhijia), Pan Gongzhan, and Gu Xinyi, totaling fourteen people. Pan Gongzhan chaired the meeting. The important agenda items of the meeting are recorded as follows: (1) The proposal to organize a fundraising team to actively raise funds was passed. The temporary fundraising methods of the committee were approved and submitted to the Municipal Government for approval and record, and active fundraising will be carried out. (2) The proposal on how to properly plan effective methods for collecting outstanding donations from various organizations was resolved to have the committee send another letter to urge payment, and each committee member will be responsible for urging payment separately. (3) The proposal to use money as the basis for the sale of fair-priced rice at distribution points and to temporarily set the selling price at 420 cash per liter (equivalent to 14 yuan per stone) was approved. (4) The proposal to suspend business for five days during the month-end commercial account closing period, starting from June 2, because most of the staff at the distribution points are partners of rice shops and have fulfilled their obligations, and the affairs of each main store are more complicated, was discussed. It was decided to allow the suspension of business for three days, from May 30 to May 31 and June 1, and the Social Affairs Bureau will make a public announcement. (5) The proposal to select Dapu Bridge and Tanzi Bay in Zhabei as locations for additional distribution points was resolved. After investigation, it was confirmed that the two locations are densely populated areas for the common people, and it was approved to open them after selecting houses and arranging them properly.

New Portuguese and French Envoys to Arrive in China

The new Portuguese envoy to China, Pa Te-si, boarded the French postal ship Lunpu in Marseille on the 24th of last month and is expected to arrive in Shanghai on the 26th of this month. The Shanghai Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs received a letter from the Portuguese consul yesterday informing them that when the new Portuguese envoy arrives in Shanghai, he will disembark at the Luhe Dock in Hongkou. It is said that Director Chen plans to go to the port to welcome him at that time.

According to diplomatic sources, the new French envoy to China, Wei Erdun, has left Marseille and is expected to arrive in Shanghai soon.

Progress of Radio Broadcasting Station

The Radio Broadcasting Station established by the General Administration of Radio of the Ministry of Communications in this city is currently in progress. It is said that the future site will be located either on Maigen Road or Fenglin Bridge. The bureau has already drafted the rules for user installations and will submit them to the ministry for approval soon. Other investigations into radio users nationwide are also underway. According to the Engineering Section of the bureau yesterday, the completion of all these matters and the commencement of broadcasting will have to wait until the autumn of this year.

Municipal Party Department

To Establish a Steering Committee

The Training, Propaganda, and Organization Departments of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department, in view of the uneconomical use of time and resources and the inconsistent leadership materials in the past when attending meetings to guide lower-level Party departments, have been planning for a long time and have decided to jointly organize a Steering Committee composed of the guidance sections of the three departments. It is said that the first conversation meeting was held on the 21st of this month, and the personnel are composed of the secretaries of each department, all the staff of the guidance section, and other staff from various offices and district committee members. The task of the committee is to unify the guidance materials and allocate the personnel attending. At the same time, for the sake of facilitating work, a presidium of three people will be set up, with the directors of the three sections serving as chairmen to direct everything. Once the organizational regulations are drafted and submitted to the Municipal Executive Committee for approval, they can be implemented.

Suppressing

Usurious Interest Rates in Concession Pawnshops

Propose Amending the Regulations on Pawnshop Licenses of the Public Works Department

The usurious exploitation of pawnshops in the concessions of this city has been a long-standing practice. Some charge interest as high as eight or nine percent per month, and six percent per month is considered normal, which is related to the livelihood of the common people. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau has now decided to suppress it according to law. The letter is recorded as follows: The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau sent a letter to the Five Chinese Directors yesterday, saying: "With regard to the case of the business rules for the pawnshop industry in this city, previously approved by the Shanghai Merchant Group Rectification Committee, which forwarded the request from the Commercial Pawnshop Association to amend the business rules for pawnshops in this city, the pawnshop business rules were revised and submitted to the National Government for approval and record, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government was ordered to instruct the former Shanghai Provisional Court to comply with the rules. The suppression of usurious exploitation is a matter of national government orders and should be strictly followed to relieve the people's difficulties. Now, all pawnshops in the Chinese territory of this city have been registered and are charging interest in accordance with the regulations. However, pawnshops in the concessions still rely on foreign forces for protection and have refused to comply. If they are not strictly suppressed, the poor people in the concessions will feel the pain, and the disparity between the Chinese and concession areas will damage national prestige. In addition to sending a separate letter to the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, we also request you to propose amending the Regulations on Pawnshop Licenses of the Public Works Department at the next meeting of the board of directors, so that all pawnshops must comply with the revised pawnshop business rules of this city approved by the National Government, reduce interest rates, and determine compensation, in order to benefit the poor and value government orders. This is our sincere hope."

The Taxpayers' Association sent a letter to the Director-General of the Public Works Department and the Five Chinese Directors, saying: "With regard to the case approved by the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau in Official Letter No. 3824, regarding the Pawnshop Business Rules of this city, which were previously sent to your association for reference, and requested that you urge the pawnshop industry in the concession to comply with them. This year, after considering commercial conditions and accommodating the opinions of the industry, slight revisions were made and submitted to the Executive Yuan of the National Government for record, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government was ordered to instruct the former Shanghai Provisional Court to comply with the rules. The suppression of usurious exploitation is a matter of national government orders and should be strictly followed to relieve the people's difficulties. Now, all pawnshops in the Chinese territory of this city have been registered within the deadline and are charging interest in accordance with the regulations. Pawnshops in the concession should not be treated differently. Therefore, we are sending another letter to your association for reference and requesting that you immediately inform the Public Works Department of the Public Concession and instruct all pawnshops in the concession to comply with the regulations strictly. We also ask you to consult with the Chinese directors to propose amending the Regulations on Pawnshop Licenses of the Public Works Department at the next meeting of the Public Works Department, and to clearly stipulate that interest should be charged in accordance with the revised pawnshop business rules of this city to benefit the poor. This is our public concern. In addition to replying to the letter and sending separate letters, we are forwarding this letter to you and hope that you will take it into consideration and implement it, and please inform us of the progress." Addressed to Mr. Edward, Director-General of the Public Works Department of the Public Concession, and Directors Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, Xu Xinliu, Bei Songsun, and Liu Hongsheng.

The Songbao Party and government, naval, army, police, and various agencies held the second joint defense meeting at the Wusong Chamber of Commerce Assembly Hall yesterday at 1:00 PM. Announcement by the Municipal Civil Training Committee

Organizational Procedures for Industrial and Commercial Trade Unions

The organizational procedures for industrial and commercial trade unions in the Shanghai Special Municipality have been promulgated and implemented by the Municipal Civil Training Committee. The original text is as follows: (1) To initiate the organization of a trade union, a joint signature of more than 50 people in the same industry is required to elect representatives, prepare a letter of justification and a resume of the initiators (the resume form should be obtained from the committee), in duplicate, and apply to the committee for permission. However, if there are fewer than 50 people in the same industry within the city, an application for permission can be made with the joint signature of one-third of the same industry or more than seven households. (2) After accepting the application, the committee will immediately send personnel to inspect, with the following key points: (1) Whether the reasons presented are justified and accurate; (2) Whether the initiators are loyal and are in the same industry; (3) Whether there is the same organization in the industry; (4) Whether there is a need to organize. (3) After receiving the report from the inspectors, the committee will review and approve whether to allow the establishment and notify the Social Affairs Bureau for reference. (4) After the trade union receives the committee's approval, it should immediately send personnel to the committee to collect the permit. (5) The trade union that has been approved to prepare should elect five to ten preparatory members to form a preparatory committee and submit it to the committee and the Social Affairs Bureau for record. The committee may send specialists to guide it when necessary. (6) During the preparation period, the preparatory committee should engrave the preparatory committee seal according to the name set by the committee. The pattern should be 1.5 inches square according to the construction foot, with each side being two inches, and the text should read "Shanghai Special Municipality XX Trade Union Preparatory Committee Seal." The text should be in seal script, and the start date and seal impression should be reported for record. (7) The preparation period for the trade union is limited to 40 days after the preparatory committee is recorded. During the preparation period, the draft constitution and membership list (the style of the constitution and membership list should be in accordance with the committee's regulations) should be submitted to the committee for review. (8) The constitution of the trade union should state the following items: 1. Name and location; 2. Matters to be handled; 3. Regulations on organization and staff; 4. Regulations on meetings; 5. Regulations on joining and expulsion of members; 6. Fundraising and revenue and expenditure methods; 7. Disciplinary methods for violations of the constitution other than expulsion; 8. The period of establishment of the trade union. (9) After the draft constitution and membership list of the trade union are approved by the committee, a founding meeting should be convened immediately and the committee should be requested to send personnel to guide it. (10) After the trade union is established, a list of the union's staff should be filled out immediately, and the changes in the constitution and membership list should be reported to the committee. After sending personnel to review it and deem it sound, the committee will issue a certificate to the union and notify the Social Affairs Bureau for reference. (11) The trade union reorganized according to the Commercial Rectification Committee's Industrial and Commercial Trade Union Rectification Procedures should immediately submit the certificate, along with the union's constitution, membership list, staff resume, and other investigation forms (the style must be in accordance with the committee's

中華民國十九年

regulations) to the committee for the committee to issue a certificate in accordance with the above procedures. (12) After the trade union receives the committee's approval for the above-mentioned certification of soundness, it should immediately apply to the Social Affairs Bureau for registration in accordance with the Shanghai Special Municipality Industrial Organization Registration Rules. (13) If a trade union has any of the following circumstances, it should submit it to the committee for approval and record at any time: 1. The date of convening the members' meeting or the representatives' meeting; 2. Re-election of staff; 3. Changes in property; 4. Fundraising activities; 5. Punishment or expulsion of members; 6. Reorganization or dissolution. (14) These organizational procedures shall be promulgated and implemented by the committee.

Investigation

Impersonation of Northeast Representative Bao Guancheng

Regarding the news in the newspapers a few days ago that Bao Guancheng, alias Qiyuan, was dispatched by the Northeast as a representative to visit a certain president in Beijing, Qin Hua, the representative of the Northeast stationed in Beijing, inquired by telegram to the Northeast authorities, who replied that no representative had been dispatched. After receiving the telegram, Qin believed that his actions were close to swindling and has telegraphed the Shanghai authorities to investigate the matter strictly.

Silk Cocoon Guild Requests Protection for Cocoon Trading

The Shanghai Special Municipality Silk Filature Association and the Joint Silk Cocoon Guild of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui, noting that the location outside Yaohua Gate in Nanjing is relatively remote, and that the newly opened Minfeng Cocoon Trading Company is about to commence trading, are deeply concerned about potential disturbances by local ruffians. They have recently sent separate telegrams to the Jiangning County Government, requesting special protection. The original telegram stated: "To the esteemed Jiangning County Government, regarding the proposal by Standing Committee Member Zhu Jing'an that to improve the silk industry and promote foreign trade, the Minfeng Model Silk Filature was established in Wuxi, and over one hundred mu of land was purchased in Yaohua Gate, Nanjing, to establish the Minfeng Seed Production Farm and the Minfeng Cocoon Trading Company, in order to improve seed production and facilitate cocoon sales for cocoon farmers. The County Government has already issued a license. However, as the market is about to open for cocoon collection, we are deeply concerned that local thugs may cause trouble. We respectfully request the Jiangning County Government to issue a proclamation and dispatch officers to provide protection. As the Minfeng Cocoon Trading Company is scheduled to open within one or two days, the matter concerns the protection of agriculture and commerce, and prevention is essential. Therefore, we respectfully request your approval to dispatch officers or guards to protect the Minfeng Cocoon Trading Company and issue a proclamation strictly prohibiting disturbances. We would be immensely grateful. Respectfully, Shen Huachen, Chairman of the Shanghai Special Municipality Silk Filature Association, and Huang Jin, Chairman of the Joint Silk Cocoon Guild."

Zhejiang Spring Cocoons Begin Transport to Shanghai

This year's Zhejiang spring cocoons transported via the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway have been loaded and transported by the Huitong Transport Company since the 12th of this month. Approximately 5,000 packages have been successively reported for shipment from the Gongchen and Chang'an stations and transported to the Shanghai South Station. Over 100 packages have also arrived at the North Station. It is reported that about 15,000 to 16,000 packages are stored in warehouses at Gongchen, Chang'an, Linping, Xucun, and other stations, awaiting transport to Shanghai. However, the Railway Bureau lacks locomotives, so extra cars are added to the Hangzhou-bound freight trains for transport. Once locomotives are available, special trains will be added to transport the cocoons to Shanghai.

Ministry Approves

Exemption of Inspection for Domestic Goods

The Ministry of Industry and Commerce's Commodity Inspection Conference previously resolved to divide the methods for inspecting goods that should be inspected into two categories: (1) Those that should be thoroughly inspected: these items, regardless of whether they are exported abroad, imported from abroad, or sold in collection and distribution markets, must be inspected uniformly. (2) Those that should be temporarily partially inspected: these items are only inspected for export, and are not inspected when transported from one port to another or sold in collection and distribution markets, except when merchants request and the Ministry specifically approves. The Ministry designated tung oil and cotton as items for thorough inspection, and livestock products and by-products, raw silk, tea, and beans as items for partial inspection, and instructed the local commodity inspection bureaus to record them. The Ministry now considers that merchants transporting pig intestines from Tianjin, Qingdao, and other places to Shanghai still need to be inspected, which would require paying fees for inspection in Shanghai, and the procedures are cumbersome, increasing the burden. This has caused some complaints. According to the resolutions of the Commodity Inspection Conference and the Ministry's orders, this is not in compliance. Therefore, the Ministry issued another order to all bureaus that casings are one of the by-products of livestock, and should be exempted from inspection when transported from one domestic port to another. It is now stipulated that, starting from today, all goods that should be partially inspected shall only be inspected for direct export abroad, unless merchants request and the Ministry specifically approves. They are exempted from inspection when transported from one port to another or sold in collection and distribution markets.

The case of foreign residents in Zhabei paying property tax has been properly negotiated by the North Municipal Tax Collection Office. The Special Municipal Finance Bureau officially issued an order yesterday to assign personnel to collect summer property tax, which is 10% for residential properties and 10% for shops. Detailed rules will be specified separately.

No Agency May Destroy Them on Its Own

The Ministry of Communications Instructed the Postal Administration to Comply Yesterday

The General Post Office of this port received instructions from the Ministry of Communications yesterday, stating: "Regarding the handling of matters, it was found that the Anti-Opium Committee had previously consulted, as instructed by the Executive Yuan and approved by the National Government, on the disposal of a large quantity of heroin seized at the post office, proposed by the Qingdao Municipal Party Committee Designated Committee. Item 3 should be changed to transferring the case to the court for execution of destruction. We hereby consult you to instruct the General Post Office to comply. Nanyang Workers Appeal for Factory Reopening

Requesting the Municipal Party Committee to Order the Factory to Resume Operations Immediately

The Nanyang Brothers Tobacco Company in this city previously announced its closure due to high gold prices, leaving thousands of workers unemployed. After investigation by the Municipal Party Committee in conjunction with the Social Affairs Bureau, it was determined that the factory had no reason to close. Therefore, four measures were decided: (1) The factory must submit its factory regulations, employment contracts, and reopening plan to the bureau for review by the end of April. (2) The factory must reopen by May 16. (3) Long-term workers who are laid off by the employer after reopening, if they have served for more than two years, must be compensated with two months' severance pay. (4) If the factory does not reopen by May 16, the factory must pay one-third of the workers' wages as a maintenance fee for the extended period. However, the factory refused to accept this ruling and appealed to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce then consulted the municipal government, stating that the above measures were inappropriate. Now, the workers have submitted a petition to the Municipal Party Committee, requesting that it maintain the original text, as follows: "Petition: Requesting that you forward to the Municipal Government and then to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, and not allow the Nanyang employer to make a one-sided request and disregard the plight of thousands of workers. The Nanyang employer has illegally closed the factory for several months, and the workers are suffering from hunger and cold. We have repeatedly requested your association and the Social Affairs Bureau to find ways to provide relief. We were then instructed to recognize that the factory's closure was a temporary suspension, not a permanent closure, and to give the company two months to reorganize and resume operations. All severance payments to workers should be considered as living expenses. Under the order of your association, we advised the workers to wait quietly for a resolution. Unexpectedly, the employer used the concession as a shield, deliberately disobeying orders and delaying the reopening of the factory. Last month, the Social Affairs Bureau instructed the factory to reopen before May 16. If it is necessary to reduce the scope of operations and lay off employees, severance pay should be paid to the workers in accordance with the law. If the factory does not reopen by then, one-third of the workers' maintenance fees should continue to be paid. Our association is in a difficult and arduous situation. Fortunately, we have received the protection of our superiors, and we are extremely grateful. Unexpectedly, the employer disregarded government orders and was insincere, submitting a report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, overturning all the methods that your association and the Social Affairs Bureau had painstakingly maintained for the workers, and considering the third party to be unreasonably interfering, attempting to erase the facts and put the lives of thousands of our workers in a desperate situation. The Ministry of Industry and Commerce also relied solely on the employer's one-sided remarks, and hastily sent a letter to the municipal government overturning the Social Affairs Bureau's solution, which is deeply regrettable. Upon investigation, the employer's report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce stated that it had paid the workers two months' severance pay, with the signature of the labor representative as proof, which may have legal effect. However, it is not known that the labor representative is an unscrupulous worker bribed by the employer, and a member of an illegal labor-management cooperation committee, which has long been rejected by the overall situation of the workers. Moreover, what was received was clearly a maintenance fee, not severance pay, but the employer actually used it as a basis, and regarded your association and the Social Affairs Bureau as an unreasonable interference by a third party. The act of deceiving superiors and misleading subordinates is extremely hateful. Our association has struggled for several months and finally achieved a glimmer of a solution, which was almost completely overturned by the employer. All the workers are extremely shocked. Now, as we are about to die, we can only make a final appeal, begging your association to understand the pain of the workers, uphold the laws of the party and the country, and, based on the facts, forward this to the municipal government, and not be blinded by the employer's one-sided reasons, which would lead to the livelihood of thousands of workers being in a desperate situation. We also hope that the employer will be ordered to open the factory immediately, so as to maintain the dying lives of the workers. We will repay your great kindness with a ring and grass. Weeping and expressing our words, we cannot help but wait for your orders. Sincerely submitted,"

National Chamber of Commerce

Requests Clemency for Yu Yaoxi's Unjust Imprisonment

The National Chamber of Commerce Federation yesterday submitted a document to the Judicial Yuan of the National Government, stating that Yu Yaoxi had no counter-revolutionary acts and requesting that the Supreme Court declare him innocent in accordance with the law. The reasons stated were roughly that Yu Yaoxi, the former president of the Jinan Commercial Port Chamber of Commerce, was detained on suspicion of counter-revolutionary crimes. The Higher Court of the province prosecuted him and sentenced him to ten years of imprisonment and deprivation of public rights for life. Recently, merchants from various ports came to the association, stating that when Zhang Zongchang occupied Shandong, Yu Yaoxi served as the president of the chamber of commerce. He had no choice but to be cordial with the warlords in order to protect himself and take care of the interests of the business community. This kind of hardship was shared by all merchants who had been under warlords. However, the Shandong Higher Court did not have any other conclusive evidence of Yu Yaoxi's crimes, and instead used his daily interactions and notices with Zhang Zongchang, and his maintenance of Shandong banknotes as evidence of rebellion, and punished him with a long-term prison sentence under the law for punishing counter-revolutionaries. If this case becomes final, all chambers of commerce that had been under warlords will not be spared. They asked the association to uphold justice and appeal on their behalf so that they can be vindicated. The association explained each point, hoping that the authorities would forgive him. Finally, they stated that Yu Yaoxi was a Christian and a staff member of the Jinan YMCA. He had been engaged in business for decades and never interfered in politics. He was usually enthusiastic about social undertakings and led the business community to compete with foreigners, so he was respected by the Shandong business community. Since his arrest and imprisonment last July, nearly a year has passed. His business has been abandoned, and the business community has lost its mentor and is extremely confused. Therefore, we hereby submit the actual situation, asking your court to quickly order the Supreme Court to expedite the declaration of innocence in accordance with the law. If the court adopts our appeal and clearly understands that the original judgment applied the wrong law, but still returns the case to the original trial in accordance with ordinary procedures, then the transfers back and forth will inevitably cause Yu Yaoxi to be imprisoned for several years, which would be a wrongful detention and would violate the government's original intention of loving the people and the court's duty to deliver justice. We still ask that this intention be communicated to the Higher Court. We are in fear and trembling, and we cannot help but to be loyal subjects."

More News from This Port Transferred to the Following Page

Page 15

May 22, 1920, Republic of China (Shen Bao Fourth Edition) Thursday (15)

News from This Port Two

Dark Side of the "Board and Lodging" Labor System

Pitiable Women from Jiangbei

Tens of Thousands of Women Come to Shanghai to Work

Employers Pocket Their Wages by Providing Room and Board

Reselling and Selling Them Off is Commonplace

The Ren Huaxiang Case is Just One Example

In recent years, due to repeated famines and widespread disasters in Funing, Yancheng, Xinghua, Lianshui, Gaoyou, and other counties in Jiangbei, the people everywhere are very impoverished, and those with large families barely get enough to eat. As a result, the Jiangbei people who live in Shanghai have taken advantage of this famine to raise funds, either by inviting friends to form associations, or by borrowing money at high interest rates, and then go back to their hometowns to recruit young women. Each woman is given 30 yuan (called a settlement allowance), and it is agreed that they will be brought to Shanghai to work for a term of three years. During this period, in addition to providing food and accommodation, all wages earned are taken by the employer. When the villagers there are worried about lack of food, they are happy to receive this 30 yuan. Therefore, in the past two years, the so-called "boarding and lodging" owners in the western part of Shanghai have recruited tens of thousands of women from their hometowns to Shanghai. Once these women arrive in Shanghai, they are placed in cotton mills by the employers to work. They eat two meals a day to barely fill their stomachs. The minimum monthly wage is 13 or 14 yuan, so after deducting the cost of food, there is a surplus of 7 or 8 yuan. Each owner has dozens of women under their care, or at least a dozen, and there are many people who have become wealthy because of these women. However, there is a dark side to it, which is infuriating. Since the owners treat these women like cattle and horses to make profits, they abuse them like pimps treat prostitutes. They have to work every day without stopping. They are not allowed to go out and play other than going to the factory to work. Some even resell or sell the women off without a trace, or take the opportunity to extort money. Their lawlessness is extreme. Yesterday, Wu Chungen, a 42-year-old native of Gaoyou who lives at 11 Hefeng Lane, Robert's Road, in the west of Shanghai, went to his hometown last year and recruited 13 women, bringing them to Shanghai to work in various cotton mills. Among these 13 women, one named Ren Huaxiang was in her prime and had a beautiful appearance. Recently, Wu secretly lured her to Shanghai without paying her a settlement allowance. However, this was discovered by the woman's fiancé's mother, Qian Zhang, because she had been living in Shanghai for a long time. Qian Zhang went to the address the day before yesterday and found the woman inside, so she took her away. Wu then grabbed Qian Zhang and called the police to arrest her at the Sixth District Police Station, accusing her of forcibly taking away a female worker. Qian Zhang also counter-accused Wu of luring the woman. The district chief conducted separate inquiries. According to Wu Chungen's statement, he is 42 years old and a native of Gaoyou. The woman, Ren Huaxiang, was entrusted to him by her parents to bring her to Shanghai to work, and Qian Zhang dared to forcibly take her away. He requested a thorough investigation. According to the woman, Ren Huaxiang, she is 20 years old and was tricked into coming to Shanghai by Wu last year. Her parents did not know about it. There were 13 women who were tricked into coming to Shanghai together. According to Qian Zhang, she is 48 years old and lives at 151 Xinkang Lane, Jiaxing Road. The woman, Ren Huaxiang, is the fiancée of her second son, and they are about to get married, so she was lured to Shanghai by Wu. She requested a thorough investigation. After obtaining the statements, the district chief found that the statements of both parties conflicted, so he immediately prepared a document and transferred it to the court for trial.

Bizarre and Absurd

A Woman's Pitiful Plea

A Person Endures Being Two Men's Wife

Failed Attempt to Sell Leads to Poisoning

Bound to a Tree, Kicked and Punched

Villagers Arrive to Rescue and Revive

Yesterday morning around 4 a.m., near the Mujia Bridge in Zhabei, on the vacant land beside the Coal Dust Road, a middle-aged woman with a face like a pigeon and covered in mud was crawling along, kneeling and pleading to the police officer on duty at the fifth precinct of the fifth district: "I have been plotted against and harmed; please investigate and do justice," she said. The officer immediately took her to the station, where she identified herself as Zhang Zhou, a 31-year-old from Funing. Her husband's name is Zhang Huilian. They had been married for five years and lived in harmony, but recently he suddenly disliked my appearance and inability to bear children and wanted to leave me. However, I lost my parents at a young age and relied on my own hands to make a living, so I did not feel bitter. I originally intended not to marry again, but Zhang Huilian repeatedly begged me, and I finally agreed. I had hoped to be faithful to him until the end, but Zhang became tired of me over time, abandoned me halfway, secretly went to Suzhou, and privately transferred me to Tan San and Zhou Si Lang to be their wife. Due to financial difficulties, I endured being the shared wife of Tan and Zhou. Who knew that my fate would be so unfortunate? Tan and the others then wanted to sell me for money, but I swore I would not comply, which caused them to harbor resentment and plot against me. Last night after dinner, I was first raped in turns, and then they lured me outside, pretending to admire the night scenery. When we reached a vacant lot, they pushed me down. Zhou took out a thick rope and tightly bound it around my chest and neck, while Tan held my arms and tied me backward to a large tree. They kicked and punched me until I was suffocating. They then leisurely left. Fortunately, a villager passed by carrying vegetables and rescued me. It took half an hour for me to wake up and thankfully, I was revived." After giving her statement, she was panting like an ox, and when she bared her upper body, there was indeed a rope mark about a foot long, with bloodstains clearly visible. The chief of police examined her statement and found it overly absurd. He observed her demeanor, which resembled that of a madwoman. However, the rope marks on her chest and neck were definitely not fabricated, and her body was covered in wounds, suggesting that she had been plotted against and harmed. The case was quite bizarre, so he immediately prepared a document and sent it to the judicial section for review.

On the Big Lai Steamer

Chinese Woman's Coffin Awaits Collection

Zhang Yapei, a Woman from Suzhou

Worked as a Servant in America, Developed Mental Illness

Suddenly Hanged Herself in a Locked Room

Coffin Arrives in Shanghai, No One Claims It

The American Da Lai Company's world-class giant steamer, President Taft, arrived in Shanghai on the 16th of this month, carrying a coffin in its hold. The ship docked at the Da Lai Wharf in Bailianjing, Pudong. Soon after, the ship sent people to transport the coffin to the wharf and leave it there. It has been almost a week, and no one has claimed it yet. It has now been ascertained that the deceased in the coffin is a Chinese woman named Zhang Yapei (transliteration), 32 years old, from Suzhou. She used to work as a servant in the house of an American (referred to by foreigners as "amah"). For some unknown reason, she suddenly developed mental illness in America, and her behavior became abnormal. She would laugh and cry all day long and speak incoherently. Her employer became annoyed and confined her to a locked room, hoping she would recover and return to normal. Unexpectedly, the woman suddenly hanged herself on May 1st. By the time the employer discovered her, she had already died. They immediately purchased a coffin, prepared her for burial, and reported the matter to the authorities. A letter was prepared, and the coffin was carried onto the ship and transported to China. There were no obstacles along the way, and it arrived directly in Shanghai. However, it is not known whether the deceased has any family members, and even if she does, their address and names are unknown, making it extremely difficult to find them. Therefore, it has been delayed for many days, and no one has claimed it yet. The company believes that keeping the coffin for too long is unhygienic and has sent letters to various land and water authorities to investigate and inform the family so that they can claim the coffin.

Co-habited for Seven or Eight Years

Slept in the Same Bed Only Once

Brothel Keeper Accuses Husband

Criminal Case with Civil Suit Attached

Purpose is Divorce

Defendant Denies Everything

Li Xiaolianzi, a woman from Jiangbei, opened a brothel in Shanghai and accumulated a considerable amount of ill-gotten gains. Being in the prostitution business, she embraced the idea of multiple partners. Recently, she hired a lawyer at the Special District Court to file a criminal and civil lawsuit against her husband, Li Zaichao. The criminal part concerned allegations of theft by her husband, while the civil part sought to terminate their relationship. Using a two-pronged approach, she hoped to achieve her goal of changing husbands as soon as possible. Yesterday morning, Judge Zhou Daren opened the court to hear the divorce case. According to her statement, she is 36 years old and lost both parents at a young age. She had no siblings. The defendant's mother took me in as an adopted daughter. When I turned 19, the defendant forced me into a room and slept with me, without holding a wedding ceremony. Judge Zhou asked her how many times she had slept with the defendant. She replied, "Only this once." Asked if she had given birth to a child, she said, "I had a daughter, but she died soon after." But judging by the years, she must be eleven years old. The court instructed her, "According to this calculation, you have cohabited with the defendant for seven or eight years. Your statement that you slept together only once is highly improbable." The questioning turned to the defendant, Li Zaichao, who stated that he was two years older than the plaintiff. He and she were married at the time, arranged by his mother, and a wedding ceremony was held. The plaintiff had also given birth twice. He was 32 years old when he had a son, but they all died young. The defendant's mother was also called to testify about the circumstances of their marriage. Regarding the wedding certificate, she said that it had been lost over the years and was difficult to find, so it could not be presented to the court. Then the lawyers for both the plaintiff and defendant began their arguments. The defendant's lawyer, Ye Fikang, said that the woman had been married to the defendant for nearly ten years, and now she was denying it. This was disregarding national law and corrupting social customs. He requested that her lawsuit be rejected. Judge Zhou adjourned the hearing until May 27 for sentencing.

Shanghai Performing Arts Circle

Welcomes Old Fellow Townsman

Loud Call of "Attend Court" Shakes the Roof Tiles

Humorous Conversations Fill the Occasion

The Shanghai Performing Arts Circle Joint Association, because of the performing arts elder and fellow townsman Sun Juxian, who is old and came to Shanghai, and after the Shanghai stage earnestly requested that he perform on stage, and he is about to head north soon, specially held a welcome party at 2 p.m. yesterday at the association's premises in Nine Mu Di. Those who attended included performing arts elders Niu Songshan (age 70), Wang Wenhua (age 69), Wang Hongquan (age 71), Xia Shengru (age 66), Sun Naiqing (age 64), and committee members Zhao Ruquan, Zhou Xinfang, Li Guichun, Chen Jiaxiang, Chen Jialin, Ge Huaqing, Wu Yuehua, Lin Shusen, Han Jinkui, and dozens of others. Sun arrived at the meeting at 2 p.m. After meeting with the committee members, he immediately wrote on a piece of paper, "Arrived at the meeting on May 21, 19th year of the Republic of China, Sun Juxian, at the age of only 90" with vigorous strokes. Then he entered the hall and the meeting began. Sun described in detail his past experiences in Shanghai, as vivid as a painting, without the slightest error. His mind was clear, which was admirable. There were humorous remarks from time to time, and all who heard them burst into laughter. As the meeting was about to end, he suddenly shouted "Attend Court," shaking the roof tiles. The entire hall burst into thunderous applause. The committee members proposed that Sun have a photo taken to commemorate the occasion. Sun replied that he had never had a photo taken or a film made in his life. By the time the meeting ended, the clock had struck four.

Inside a Small Teahouse

Large-Scale Flower Gambling Den Busted

Opening Gambling Three Times Day and Night

Flower Gambling Archway with Bizarre Shapes

Riddles on the Gambling Cards Are Peculiar

Chief Operator Sentenced to a Fine of 500 Yuan

The evils of flower gambling are well known. Recently, unscrupulous individuals have been opening gambling dens three times day and night. Therefore, the French Concession Police have paid close attention to this and instructed all police stations to strictly investigate and arrest those involved. On the day before yesterday at noon, the French Concession Police Detective Inspector General Shen Defu, Detective Bao Tan Shiqing, and others discovered a large-scale flower gambling den operating inside a small teahouse at No. 25 Yong'an Lane, behind Beile Road. They immediately proceeded to the address without making a sound and raided the place. At that time, the group was in the midst of gambling, in high spirits. They arrested the chief operator, Lin Yinfu, on the spot, while the others scattered and fled. They confiscated a flower gambling archway, covered with a large red satin cloth. On one side were written the words "One Hundred Taboos Are Forbidden," and on the other side were written "Kill All Sides." Red tassels were attached to both sides, and a copper plaque was placed on top with the words "Abundant Financial Resources, One Original Ten Thousand Profits." At the very top was a foreign iron tube about a foot long, containing the names of the flower gambling winners (the words "Occupying the First Place"), covered with red satin. There were also two sets of riddles written on the gambling cards, such as "Nezha Uproar in the Sea, Parents Angered, Taiyi Battles with Magic, Caishi Isle," and they also confiscated silver dollars and other items. They were taken to the police station and sent to the French Concession Court yesterday for investigation. First, Western Detective Chief Sacaier reported to the court that this type of flower gambling was completely deceptive and harmful to the people. These main dens are the most difficult to bust, but now that they have been arrested, he requested that they be severely punished. When questioned, Lin Yinfu admitted to privately opening a large flower gambling den. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Lin to a fine of 500 yuan. If he was unable to pay the fine, he would be imprisoned for 500 days as a warning. All confiscated items would be confiscated.

This Year Qingyang Port Still Prohibits Boat Races

The "North China Daily News" reports that the Shanghai Boat Association used to hold boat races at Qingyang Port in spring and autumn. Since last autumn, the provincial government has ordered the prohibition of such races, stating that Qingyang Port is located inland and is not a trading port. Therefore, the races were moved to the Chenjia Mouth area of the Huangpu River. This spring, the association chairman submitted a request to the provincial government, asking to be allowed to hold the races at Qingyang Port as before. Recently, Chairman Ye rejected the request and telegraphed the Kunshan County government to take note.

Japanese Consulate

Three Koreans Sentenced to Deportation

The "Great Evening News" reports that the three Koreans who were arrested in the French Concession at the end of last month were sentenced yesterday (the 20th) after being sent to the Japanese Consulate General. They were found guilty of disturbing the peace and were ordered to be deported to their home country. They were scheduled to be escorted onto the Nagasaki Maru this morning (the 21st) to be transported back to Japan.

Huining Compatriots Organize Rice Relief for Famine

The Huining Shanghai Compatriot Association convened a joint meeting of all executive committee members and various county compatriot associations the day before yesterday. Wang Yucheng chaired the meeting. The chairman first reported on (1) the rice famine in their hometowns, and the letters and telegrams from various counties; (2) the letter from the Xiuning Association, reporting the steps taken to organize rice relief for the famine; (3) welcoming the representatives from Tunxi, Mr. Liu Ziyuan, the representative from Qimen, Mr. Chen Xizhe, and the representative from Wuyuan, Mr. Pan Zhiren, who reported on the famine situation in their respective counties. Next, they discussed (1) the association decided to use all the remaining funds from last year's disaster relief to organize rice relief for the famine. The resolution was unanimously approved; (2) responsible personnel were publicly elected to handle the rice relief. Yu Langxi, Hu Peiru, Huang Yuding, Xu Xiaofu, and Shu Liwang were selected to be responsible for the handling, and Hu Fuhua and Xu Xiaofu were nominated to carry the documents overnight to the National Government Relief Committee to apply for tax-exempt passports to facilitate transportation; (3) 2,000 bags of Saigon rice would be organized first and transported to the counties most in need of disaster relief for immediate assistance. The meeting adjourned at around 8 p.m.

Baoshan Establishes Poor Farmers' Loan Office

Wu Jia, the magistrate of Baoshan County, convened a joint meeting of the heads of various bureaus and district chiefs under his jurisdiction in the county government's conference hall at 1 p.m. yesterday to discuss the establishment of a poor farmers' loan office. Magistrate Wu chaired the meeting. The resolutions are recorded below: (1) In order to relieve impoverished farmers in the county, a temporary poor farmers' loan office will be established to provide loans for farmers to purchase seeds and farming tools, limited to those who cultivate five acres or less; (2) The base fund is set at 2,500 yuan, and it was resolved that the finance bureau will temporarily transfer funds from the land tax to cover it; (3) The county government entrusts the district branches with the responsibility of handling the loan matters, with each district allocated 500 yuan; (4) The maximum loan amount for a poor farmer is 10 yuan, with a monthly interest rate of 5%; (5) Poor farmers requesting loans must find reliable guarantors to fill out loan agreements; (6) The loan repayment period is once after the autumn harvest, no later than the end of December this year. Overdue payments will be the responsibility of the original guarantor; (7) After recovering the principal and interest, each district office should immediately return it to the county government; (8) If there are any matters not covered by these measures, a meeting may be convened to revise them; (9) These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the county government; (10) The date of establishment of the poor farmers' loan office is set for June 1.
