Public Works Bureau Inspects Public Buses

To Be Held in Six Phases

In order to rectify traffic and ensure the safety of passengers, the Municipal Public Works Bureau requires all vehicles to pass inspection before they are allowed to operate. Recently, due to the large capacity and large number of passengers of public buses, it is particularly necessary to conduct periodic inspections. Therefore, a rotating inspection method has been established. The main points are: (1) All vehicles owned by each company will be equally distributed, and inspections will be carried out every two months on a rotating basis. The bureau will send personnel to each company every week to handle the inspections, for a total of six inspection phases per year. The bureau will prepare a schedule of inspection dates in advance and issue it to the companies. The companies will distribute the vehicles evenly, fill in the vehicle numbers, report them to the bureau, and the bureau will send personnel to inspect them daily. (2) All vehicles to be inspected must be repainted and repaired completely in advance. (3) Vehicles that fail the inspection will have their licenses revoked and will not be returned until they pass a re-inspection. (4) All vehicles prepared for inspection must be parked in the factory awaiting inspection according to the listed schedule. It is understood that the above measures will be implemented from June 1. The bureau has issued the forms to the Huashang Hunan and Public Bus Companies and instructed them to distribute the vehicles, fill in the vehicle numbers, and submit them for record.

Pharmacies Must Display Prescription Dispensing Hours

The Shanghai Special City New Pharmaceutical Industry Association sent a letter to its member pharmacies, stating: "Greetings, we have recently received a letter from the Shanghai Medical Association stating that at our association's spring conference on April 27, it was resolved that pharmacies should specify prescription dispensing hours for patients. This matter has been handed over to the executive committee to discuss appropriate measures and notify all pharmacies in this city to implement them immediately in order to benefit patients and fulfill their duties." Our association's executive committee has already agreed on appropriate measures on the 4th of this month. We are now sending them to you and hope that your association will adopt them and inform all pharmacies to follow them. A copy of the appropriate measures is enclosed for your reference. The measures state: "In the future, all pharmacies in this city must display their weekday prescription dispensing hours on their doors so that patients can know which pharmacy should dispense prescriptions during certain hours and avoid making futile trips and delaying treatment. For example, those who only dispense prescriptions during the day should specify the time from when to when, and those who also dispense at night can mark 'Day and Night Prescription Dispensing'. A responsible pharmacist must be stationed to provide service during the specified hours and must not leave without authorization."

More HSBC Counterfeit Notes Discovered

Ten Yuan Notes Altered to One Hundred Yuan

Two Men and Women Arrested for Using Them

HSBC's ten-yuan notes, altered to one hundred yuan, were used in the city, and the police arrested two women for using these altered banknotes, and sent them to the Special District Court for trial, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Unexpectedly, at around 6 p.m. the night before, Fang Chongrong from Guangdong and Yang Chen from Guangdong attempted to exchange the ten-yuan note altered to one hundred yuan at Shen Chengzhang's tobacco and paper shop at No. 1031 Yalv Road. Shen discovered the alteration and called the police. Fang escaped in the commotion, but Yang Chen was apprehended, along with the altered note, and taken to the Hongkou Police Station. Fang later returned near the tobacco and paper shop, hoping to gather information, but was spotted by Shen, who called the police and had him arrested. Yesterday morning, both were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Feng conducted the trial. First, Chen, an HSBC employee, stated that the paper of the counterfeit notes was rough and the patterns were different from those of genuine notes. When questioned, the two defendants gave evasive answers, but according to the police investigation, Fang Chongrong had been convicted of using counterfeit notes before. He was now a repeat offender, and they requested severe punishment. The court ordered the defendants to be detained and await sentencing.

Transfer of Kidnappers from Donghui

Yu Genlin, a villager from Sanzao, Pudong, was kidnapped by bandits on the 5th of this month and disappeared without a trace. Subsequently, his family received a ransom letter from the bandits, asking to meet near the Great World in the French Concession, holding five cigarettes as a signal. The family reported this to the Nanhui County Public Security Bureau. Detective Chief Tang Yunzhong and the victim's family came to Shanghai and reported it to the French Concession Police, who dispatched detectives to assist in waiting near the Great World. Following the plan, two bandits, Ye Gengsheng and Zhang Asan, came to meet them. The detectives arrested Ye and Zhang and took them to the police station, as reported in yesterday's newspaper. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the French Concession Court for interrogation. First, the detectives stated the case and requested that they be transferred back to the case for interrogation. When questioned, Ye and Zhang both claimed to be from Pudong and that they had come to Shanghai to look for friends, denying that they were bandits. The Chinese and Western judges approved the transfer of the two defendants to the detectives to be taken back to the case for interrogation.

Trial and Sentence for French Woman Injured in Car Accident

Compensation of One Hundred and Fifty Yuan

A French woman, Madame Blanc, was riding in a rickshaw last month when it was hit by a car driven by rickshaw driver Yu Kaitang at the intersection of Nanjing Road and Sichuan Road in the British Concession. Madame Blanc fell out of the rickshaw and was seriously injured. She was sent to the hospital for treatment and hired a lawyer to represent her and file a lawsuit in the French Concession Court, requesting compensation for damages. After hearing the case, the court announced the end of the debate and adjourned for review and judgment. Yesterday, the Chinese and Western judges ruled that Yu should be fined 15 yuan and compensate the plaintiff 150 yuan for damages.

Workers' Brawl Dispersed by Police

Two People Apprehended on the Spot

At around 7 p.m. the night before, more than 20 people resembling workers suddenly gathered near Sanguantang, Yangjiazhai, Pudong, each holding axes and iron bars, intending to engage in a brawl. One person held a handgun and fired five or six shots outward from inside a bamboo fence. The patrol captain of the Third District Public Security Bureau, Police Officer X, happened to be passing by and went to investigate after hearing the shots. The group, seeing the unfavorable situation, scattered and fled. Two people, Lu Agen from Tongzhou and Xu Qingzhi from Suqian, were apprehended on the spot, and more than a dozen bullets were recovered at the scene. Xu Qingzhi had a gunshot wound on the upper part of his right thigh, with the bullet passing through, leaving a bloodstained hole. He was sent to the Pudong Hospital for treatment. Lu Agen was temporarily detained pending investigation of the actual circumstances of the incident.

Handgun Found on a Woman

Also a Found Opium Pipe

The guard at the gate of the Fifth District Police Station in Zhabei saw an old woman accompanied by three men the day before yesterday. Their expressions were flustered and suspicious. He knew they were not good people at a glance and immediately detained them and searched them. Two handguns were found on the woman. He then took the woman and the three men to the police station and reported to the chief. The woman identified herself as Gu Wang, from Funing, and said that she lived at Yaojia Stone Bridge in Zhabei. The guns belonged to Chen Pei, who asked her and the three men to deliver them to a buyer because women are more reliable and can avoid the trouble of searches. One of the three men, Yang Junchuan, Chen A'er, and Ding Baogui, gave similar statements. The station then ordered the police to arrest Chen Pei, but he had already fled. They then searched the homes of the defendants and found opium pipes and other items. They were all presented to the Public Security Bureau, which transferred them to the District Court for questioning yesterday.

Seven-Year-Old Girl Pawned for Thirty Silver Dollars

Heartless Concubine

Trial and Transfer to Court

A'feng, the seven-year-old daughter of Ni Xueyun, a worker at the Dongjiadu Match Factory in Pudong, was abducted by Wu Zheng, the concubine of Ni's brother, Ni Xueqing, in collusion with Chen Shugen on September 22 last year. Ni filed a complaint with the Third Precinct of the Third Sub-station, which arrested Chen and sent him to the District Court for trial. Wu, however, fled. Ni later learned that Wu had fled to Huzhou and remarried to the owner of a shoe store named Lu An in the South Gate of Huzhou. He went there the day before yesterday and found Wu, bringing her back to Shanghai. He filed a complaint with the Third Precinct of the Third Sub-station. Wu confessed that after taking the child, she could not sell her, so she pawned her at the Wu Ji Kee store in Nanhu Tou, Pinghu, for 30 silver dollars, with Yao as the mediator, who could redeem her. As the case involved abduction, they were immediately transferred to the District Court for questioning.

Demand Extortion Case by Laid-Off Workers

Transferred from Simple Court to Local Court

Plaintiff Requests Prosecution Under Criminal Law

Zhang Zi'an, manager of the Samsung Cotton and Iron Factory, was attacked and injured by Wang Kehua, a laid-off worker from the factory, at the entrance of the Yuxing Lane on Nanjing Road. The police arrested Wang and sent him to the Special District Court, where Judge Shen Shumu of the Simple Criminal Court ordered him to be detained pending further investigation, as reported in the previous newspaper. Since being fired, the worker had repeatedly used threatening means to extort money from Zhang. Now, Zhang Zi'an hired lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a lawsuit, requesting that he be punished under Article 318 of the Criminal Law. As the scope of the case was broader than initially thought and the Simple Court had no jurisdiction, Judge Shen transferred the case file to the Local Court. Yesterday, Judge Xu ordered the defendant Wang Kehua to be brought in for trial. Lawyer Zhan stated the circumstances of the defendant's repeated extortion, saying that after Wang was fired by the factory, he extorted money from Zhang. He was initially given 50 yuan, but soon after, he used the same trick again. The plaintiff, considering that he was unemployed, gave him another 56 yuan, and the defendant signed a statement promising not to cause any more trouble. Unexpectedly, he became even more extreme, writing threatening letters and demanding money from the plaintiff, so he filed a complaint requesting an investigation to warn the rascals. Judge Xu questioned the defendant and ordered him to be detained and a new date set to summon witnesses for further hearings.

Robbers Gathered to Plot a Robbery and Were Arrested

Yu Changyuan, a detective from the Jing'an Temple Police Station, and a Western detective secretly went to a hotel at No. 368 Edward Road at 7 p.m. the night before and arrested three robbers: Zhang A'er and Qu Ziyu from Pudong, and Zhang A'wu from Nanxiang. Zhang A'er was found to be carrying a handgun, which was also confiscated. They were sent to the Special District Court yesterday. Detective Yu stated that the defendants were gathered at the hotel to plot a robbery, and after learning of this through investigation, they were arrested. He requested an extension to investigate the crimes they had committed. Judge Sun questioned Zhang and the others and ordered them to be detained and a new date set for trial.

Cleverly Designed Kidnapping

Brother Xing Cries Bitterly in Father's Arms

Li Hu Shi and Others Arrested

Wang Caifu, a native of Changzhou, residing at No. 442 Guangdong Road above Wu Yixing Noodle Shop, made a living selling small books and practicing "tiao sha" (a traditional healing technique). His daughter, Xingdi, was eight years old and quite clever. On the 21st day of the second month of the lunar calendar this year, a fellow villager of Wang, Wu Youdi, took Xingdi away under the pretext of watching a grand funeral procession,

Page 16

May 22nd, 19th Year of the Republic of China (Fourth Page of Shen Bao)

and her whereabouts became unknown. Wang was extremely distraught by the sudden loss of his beloved daughter and reported the matter to the British and French Concession police, requesting an investigation. Later, he remembered that Xingdi had been taken away by Wu Youdi. He brought Wu to a tea party and demanded the return of Xingdi, but Wu firmly denied any involvement in enticing or hiding Xingdi. After mediation by the crowd, a Mr. Shi, who owned a woodworking shop, vouched for Wu, and the matter was settled. In reality, Wu had hidden Xingdi in the home of his friend, Zhang Delin, with the intention of selling her for profit. After two months of waiting and seeing no action, he colluded with Zhang's mistress, Li Hu Shi, to take Xingdi to Laobaidu in Pudong yesterday morning. They boarded the Nisshin Kisen Kaisha's Songshan Maru ship to sell her abroad. At 11:00 AM, just as the ship was about to set sail, investigators Chen Shaoting and Lin Yongfang from a relief organization boarded the ship. They found Wu and Xingdi and questioned them about their background, but their answers were inconsistent. They were taken to the Water Police Station together. According to Hu Shi's statement, she was 27 years old, from Changzhou, and was taking her niece to her father's place in Xiamen. Xingdi claimed she had been renamed Yang Guiying, her age falsely reported as nine, and that her mother had passed away. She said her father, Yang Rengen, was doing business in Xiamen, and she was going there with her aunt. The police chief did not believe her and interrogated her strictly. She finally confessed the entire story of being lured away, as well as her home address. She also said that the previous statement was taught by Hu Shi. The police chief verified the statements and concluded that Hu Shi and her accomplices were involved in human trafficking, with a meticulously designed plan and devoid of humanity. He ordered Detective Ge Changsheng to bring Xingdi's father, Wang Caifu, to the police station according to the address. When Xingdi saw her father arrive, she burst into tears and hugged him. Wang was overjoyed to have his long-lost daughter returned and was moved to tears. The police chief ordered that the plaintiffs and defendants be sent to the local court for disposition.

Robbery and Shooting Last Night on Zilai Street

Fortunately No One Was Injured

Detectives Capture One Thief

Zheng Ganqing, a Chaozhou merchant, 58 years old, runs the Zheng Qiaji Foreign Goods and Grocery Store at No. 12 Shenxing Lane, near the iron gate at the southern end of Zilai Street, opposite the Big Ben in the French Concession. He has been in business for many years and enjoys a good reputation, making him a target for criminals. Yesterday evening, around 8 PM, the store's employees had just finished dinner and were closing the iron gate at the front entrance when six thieves suddenly rushed in through the back door. Three of the thieves were armed with pistols. Several employees were talking at the entrance of the west wing room. They saw the six men rush in and knew they were not good people, so they quickly retreated into the west wing room and sounded the alarm. At the same time, the thieves turned off all the lights and three thieves took out flashlights and broke into the east wing room, the accounting room, and looted cash, totaling about 1,500 yuan. Two thieves kicked open the door of the west wing room and forbade any outcry. Unexpectedly, when the alarm first sounded, nearby detectives heard the alarm and reported it to the Big Ben police station. The police station immediately mobilized more than 30 on-duty detectives and rushed to the scene by car. They surrounded the house. By that time, the thieves had already obtained the loot and fired four shots in the house as a warning, shattering a piece of glass on the front window of the west wing. As they were leaving, trying to escape, one thief was about to open fire when he reached the alley entrance, but the detectives bravely rushed forward and apprehended him, recovering both the stolen goods and the thief. They were taken to the Big Ben police station. After a strict interrogation by the police chief, he ordered the thief to be detained and sent to court for trial.

40,000 Red Pills Hidden in a Medicine Box

Impersonating a Wandering Doctor Exposed

At the Shanghai South Railway Station of the Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway yesterday morning at 8:30 AM, as the fourth express train to Hangzhou was being prepared for departure, a passenger, about 40 years old, carrying a hand bell and a medicine box on his shoulder (resembling a wandering doctor), caught the attention of Jian Huanluan, the deputy director of the Railway Police Department. Jian, along with police officers Zhong Daofan and others, stepped forward to inspect him. They found 40 boxes of red pills hidden inside the medicine box, each box containing 1,000 pills, totaling 40,000 pills. The man and the pills were detained and taken to the Police Department. After a brief interrogation by Police Chief Huang, the man identified himself as Xu Fulin, 42 years old, from Huaining County, Anhui Province. He claimed that the red pills were entrusted to him by a friend to take to Hangzhou. After Police Chief Huang verified the information, he prepared a written report and dispatched police officers to send the man and the pills to the local court for further investigation.

Minhang All Circles Practice with Fire Extinguishers

The Minhang First District Party Branch, First District Office, Chamber of Commerce, and others, taking the 20th day of the lunar fifth month as the Dragon Boat Festival, traditionally hold water dragon drills. The intention is very good. Now that the Gregorian calendar is used, all such customs should also be moved to the Gregorian calendar. Yesterday, letters were sent to all circles, gathering all the fire-fighting equipment in the town at the intersection of Jiuguo Road for a drill. Oil shops, sauce shops, rice shops, clothing shops, wood firms, and various street sections participated, with more than a thousand fire extinguishers. The equipment was sophisticated, and the water spray was very high and far-reaching. In particular, an oil shop's equipment was newly purchased and more agile. A crowd gathered to watch, applauding and cheering. It is said that District Chief Wu intends to purchase silver shields and other prizes to encourage the practice.

Zhang Xingdi Suddenly Disappears

A Ningbo Girl Arrives in Shanghai for the First Time

Zhang Afu, a farmer from Cixi, Ningbo, asked a friend in Shanghai to recommend his 11-year-old daughter, Xingdi, to the Heki Sock Factory at No. 58 Houde Lane, Lanwei Ai Road, French Concession, to learn how to sew sock toes. He accompanied his daughter to Shanghai the day before yesterday. After disembarking in the morning, he asked the recommender to send her to the factory. Because the girl was new to Shanghai, she went to play in the lane around 11:00 AM and suddenly disappeared. The people in the factory searched everywhere, but she was nowhere to be found by night. They immediately notified her family and reported the incident to the police station, requesting an investigation to find the girl. The girl speaks with a Shaoxing accent, has a round face, large eyes, and a slightly dark complexion. Her hair has been cut short. She is wearing a red striped short shirt and pants, red floral shoes, and pink socks.

Ma Piqing, also known as Zhang Yuming, was recently arrested by Detective Cao Asan of the Xinzha Police Station for a robbery case. According to Zhang's confession at the police station, Miao Ayu, a native of Wuxi, was one of his accomplices. Miao was hiding at No. 49 in Xinzha. Yesterday morning, Detective Cao and Western Detective Nai Tai secretly went to No. 49 and arrested Miao. He was sent to the Special District Local Court. It was discovered that on January 18th of this year, Miao had colluded with others, armed with weapons, to rob the home of Liang Zuozhong at No. 60 North Sichuan Road, stealing valuables worth over 130 yuan. Police lawyer Wang Yaotang explained the case and requested a postponement to consolidate it with Zhang Yuming's case for trial. The defendant also retained lawyer Fan Gang for defense. Judge Sun approved the request, and the police sent Miao back to the police station for detention.

Escorting Kidnappers of Both Genders as a Warning

Kidnappers Li Wenfu, Guo Tingqi, Sha Bingqian, and Li Xu Shi, etc., kidnapped Chen Deyou's six-year-old son, Shiai, from his residence at No. 404 Maybach Road on January 23rd this year. They were apprehended by the Huishi Police Station and sent to the Special District Local Court for investigation and trial. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Tingqi convened the court and sentenced Li Wenfu to three years in prison and fined him 500 yuan. The other three kidnappers were each sentenced to one year and six months in prison. The number of days of detention before the judgment was confirmed was allowed to offset one day of imprisonment for every two days of detention.

The National General Hall of the Self-Reliance Society Will Be Completed

The headquarters of the Chinese Jesus Self-Reliance Society, in accordance with the principle of abolishing unequal missionary treaties, purchased land entirely by Chinese in Xiangyin Road to build its national general hall. The Executive Committee has decided that the new hall will open on June 1st, holding a completion ceremony. In addition to sending invitations to various agencies and public organizations to attend and provide guidance, seven committee members, including Zhu Baoluo, Shao Changgeng, Chen Weixin, Dong Tianjue, Zhu Jinshan, Chai Lianfu, and Pang Zixian, were appointed to make preparations to ensure the event is solemn.

News from Various Labor Unions

The Shanghai Merchants Steam Navigation Company's No. 5 Wharf Workers' Union held its sixth executive committee temporary meeting yesterday to discuss the following matters: (1) The chairman proposed that since Standing Committee Member Shan Xishou has returned to work after leave, the acting Standing Committee Member Shi Hongzhang should be dismissed. The meeting decided to pass the motion. (2) The chairman proposed that the matters discussed today are related to Zhou Pingshu's own issues, and whether he could be asked to temporarily withdraw from the meeting. The meeting decided to pass the motion. (3) The Zhongzhan branch committee reported that Zhou Pingshu, Weng Qingbiao, and three other station members were dismissed by the company for using force during a joke and requested negotiations. The meeting decided (a) to negotiate with the company regarding Zhou Pingshu's matter, (b) to seriously negotiate with the company regarding Li Dehua's and Yang Deming's matters, and (c) to convene a branch committee meeting when necessary.

The New New Company Workers' Union held a general membership meeting the day before yesterday afternoon at 8:00 PM. More than 450 people attended. Yao Jinren, Wang Fuxiang, and Deng Zongnian chaired the meeting as scheduled to discuss the following matters: (1) The temporary working days on Sundays have expired, and the company is deliberately delaying. How should this be stopped? The meeting decided to submit a request to the Municipal Social Bureau for handling. (2) The company recently promulgated new regulations with extremely harsh content. How should this be dealt with? The meeting decided to submit the matter to the executive committee for review. (3) Regarding the issue of canceling employment contracts, the meeting decided to elect ten representatives to negotiate seriously with the company. (4) Regarding the company's illegal dismissal of worker Xu XX, the meeting decided to provide legal aid and to use the entire membership as a backing. (5) Regarding the rectification of discipline, the meeting decided to organize a secret investigation team. The meeting adjourned after discussion.

Incoming

Ericsson Telephone Company's Opinion

On the Advisory Committee's Report on the Sale of the China and Foreign Telephone Company

The sale of the China and Foreign Telephone Company has been reviewed by the advisory committee, which has completed its review of the bids from various potential buyers and presented its report to the public. This matter is related to the interests of telephone users and shareholders of the China and Foreign Telephone Company, so we dare to offer our opinions frankly.

The advisory committee's report stated that the standards for its decision were (1) to safeguard the interests of shareholders and (2) to safeguard the interests of users. Therefore, it is necessary to first know which bidder can improve service and completely install automatic telephones in the shortest possible time to ensure satisfaction. Thus, the advisory committee's standard for decision is to prioritize the interests of shareholders. Ericsson Company is willing to pay shareholders 100 taels of silver per share, while the International Telephone and Telegraph Company is only willing to pay 75 taels of silver per share. The advisory committee considers the price offered by the International Company to be fair. What method was used to estimate this fair price? According to Ericsson's estimate, the actual value of the China and Foreign Telephone Company's stock is 80 taels of silver per share, and the value of the company's brand and customers is 20 taels of silver per share. Is this not a fair price?

Since the advisory committee prioritizes the interests of shareholders, why does it prevent shareholders from obtaining an additional 25 taels of silver per share? The reason may be to safeguard the interests of users, but in fact, the opposite is true. The International Company requires an interest rate of 1.05% per week, while Ericsson Company requires an interest rate of 0.9%. The difference is 0.15%. By 1932, the capital that the International Company must pay is 13,100,020 taels of silver, requiring interest of 1,325,510 taels of silver. The capital that Ericsson Company must pay is 12,200,000 taels of silver, requiring interest of 1,080,000 taels of silver. The difference is 295,510 taels of silver. This annual interest of approximately 300,000 taels of silver will have to be borne by users in the future. If Ericsson Company's bid is accepted, this annual interest of approximately 300,000 taels of silver can be saved. Is this not in the interest of users?

The advisory committee considers the International Company's fast delivery to be one of its advantages. However, all three bidding companies have guaranteed their delivery dates in writing. Is our allowance for their guarantees insufficient for trust? As a matter of fact, the so-called fast delivery of the International Company refers to the central telephone exchange in this city. The order was placed in 1923, but the installation was not completed until 1927, when it could be used.

Another advantage of the International Company is that its employees are familiar with the operation of rotary automatic telephones and have received training. However, in fact, the so-called employees include only seven foreigners and fifty-nine Chinese who have received this training. The vast majority of the remaining employees will need to be trained before using this new equipment.

The advisory committee stated that the benefit presented by the International Company is the rapid improvement of telephones. However, regarding the installation and operation of Ericsson automatic telephones, which would be less expensive and could be completed within two years, the committee stated that it was not satisfied. Its distrust of Ericsson Company's ability to fulfill the bidding conditions is what we most oppose. Ericsson is a world-renowned company, and its promised conditions should be trusted by the world. During the advisory committee's inquiry, I informed them of the estimated value of the construction and proved that Ericsson-style (i.e., progressive) automatic telephones are cheaper and more economical than rotary automatic telephones in all aspects. Even the construction cost of Ericsson-style factories is less than half that of the International Company. We can compare the two telephone exchanges in Shanghai now. The East District telephone exchange is Ericsson-style and was installed in 1924. The Central District telephone exchange is rotary-style and was installed in 1927. According to Mr. Anson's opinion, the East District exchange is still in good condition and operates smoothly, while the Central District exchange, after three years of operation, requires costly repairs to operate smoothly. Therefore, after long-term testing, the advantages and disadvantages of the two exchanges have become extremely clear.

Ericsson Company also proposed using Strowger automatic telephones in its bid. However, the advisory committee stated that if Strowger-style telephones were used, the Telegraph and Telephone Trust Company would have to undertake the project. However, Ericsson Company has a large factory in Beeston, England, which manufactures Strowger-style equipment for the British Post Office. It can also cooperate with the Automatic Telephone Manufacturing Company in Liverpool, England, to ship Strowger-style equipment to China from its factory. All materials are British goods, and trained staff can be sent to manage the project. The advisory committee does not seem to have given sufficient attention to Ericsson Company's proposal and focused on the proposals of the International Company and the Trust Company, choosing between rotary-style and Strowger-style. Therefore, the advisory committee's decision is difficult to understand.

Ericsson Company has 50 years of experience in building telephone businesses around the world and is well-positioned to benefit the people of Shanghai. I am confident that you will give it due consideration and will not approve the advisory committee's report without considering it.

Imperial Chemical Industries (ICI) announces that in the local news section of the "Shen Bao" on the 15th of this month, there was an article entitled "Shantou National Products Association Bitterly Criticizes the Harm of Superphosphate Fertilizer to Agriculture," which excerpted a letter issued on behalf of Shantou soybean cake merchants. It is claimed that ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer has been tested and approved by the Agricultural Products Inspection Institute as suitable for use. However, the Shantou soybean cake merchants are suspicious because it is becoming popular. The increasing sales of ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer and the declining sales of soybean cake are actually due to farmers who have used ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer and have realized its various benefits. Ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer is made from nitrogen extracted from the air and does not contain nitric acid. Air is essential for everyone to breathe, so it cannot be said to be highly toxic. Furthermore, artificial fertilizer merchants never mention a single word against the use of organic fertilizer. They are aware that organic fertilizer is beneficial for crops, but compared to ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer, its effectiveness is weaker and slower. A better result can be achieved by using both organic and artificial fertilizers together. The letter claims that Japan, which is very advanced in agriculture, still does not use superphosphate fertilizer. This is not true. Last year, Japan imported 282,227 tons of ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer, more than twice the amount imported by China. At the same time, Japan also produces large quantities of ammonium sulfate and other artificial superphosphate fertilizers. The speed at which their imports and production increase each year is rapidly growing. It is estimated that the amount of ammonium sulfate superphosphate fertilizer used this year will reach 600,000 tons. According to customs reports for 1928, China imported 12,656,254 piculs of rice. Given the vast area of rice paddies in China, its self-sufficiency in this staple food should be better than it currently is. To remedy this and make China self-sufficient, the productivity of each mu of rice paddy must be increased. In addition to using organic fertilizer, the only way to increase production is to promote the use of artificial fertilizers, as proven to be beneficial by countries around the world. Social News

A Woman Injured by Glass Shards

Demands Over 100,000 Gold Yuan in Compensation

And Gets Her Wish

New York News: The common pleas court of Pittsburgh recently ruled on the largest individual compensation case in the area's history. The plaintiff was Miss Hain (23 years old), and the defendants were the Mellon brothers, the current U.S. Treasury Secretary. The Mellon brothers own the Pittsburgh Hotel. The hotel hired workers to build a house, and a hammer accidentally fell, breaking the glass window across the street. Miss Hain was injured by the broken glass shards, so she sued the Mellon brothers, demanding 107,427 gold yuan in compensation. After four hours of deliberation, the jury ruled that the defendants should compensate the plaintiff the amount she requested.

Pigeon Flies Faster Due to Yearning for Its Young

The Japanese 11th Division recently held joint exercises, causing 20 military pigeons to fly 3,000 meters. As a result, three pigeons reached the distance in one minute. The normal flying speed of pigeons is 1,000 meters per minute at close range, so 3,000 meters is a rare record. The pigeon team studied the anomaly. According to Lieutenant Ogawa, the pigeon team leader, all three pigeons had chicks. Perhaps they were so eager to see their young that they flew the distance in one breath.

The 15th U.S. Census

The Country Divided into 574 Districts

100,000 Enumerators Conduct Survey

Since its founding, the United States has held a national census every ten years. This survey is the best record of the country's development. This year marks the 15th census, which began last month. The federal government hired 100,000 enumerators, who were sworn in before departing to various parts of the country. In addition to population statistics, they must also compile survey forms on agriculture, water conservancy, canal distribution, unemployment, mining, and manufacturing. The completeness of the survey categories is a first. Each enumerator carries a survey form and a map of the area they are surveying (with instructions). They must personally visit each place, meet with the responsible family member, inquire about everything, and fill out the form accordingly. Those who refuse to answer questions or provide false answers will be punished according to the law, or enumerators who abuse their power and illegally disclose the information obtained will also be punished. To ensure the accuracy of the survey, the country is divided into 574 supervisory districts, and one supervisor is carefully selected for each district to oversee all survey matters. The survey form contains 24 questions, which are more detailed than in the previous survey, as follows:

(1) The relationship of each family member to the head of the household, and a description of the family's organization.

(2) Whether the family owns or rents the property.

(4) Whether the house has a wireless radio.

(5) Whether the family lives on a farm.

(6) The gender of each family member.

(7) The race or ethnicity of each family member.

(8) The age of each family member on their last birthday.

Treasures in an Egyptian Tomb

The accidental discovery of an ancient tomb in Egypt has also spread around the world. The treasures unearthed are naturally antique, especially a few rare treasures, which are the most precious. I have received this news and will introduce it to the readers.

Location of the Tomb

The tomb was discovered not far from the Sphinx in Egypt. The Sphinx is one of Egypt's ancient monuments. There is a story behind it, which I will tell you now.

According to Greek mythology, "In the past, there was a female monster with wings, a human face, and a lion's body. She sat on a rock by the roadside and asked passersby a riddle: 'What has four legs in the beginning, then two legs, and then three legs? The one with the most legs is the youngest?' If they couldn't answer, she would kill them. Later, a man named Oedipus said, 'It is a human. Because when humans are born, they use their hands and feet to practice walking, so they have four legs. When they grow up, they walk on two legs. When they get old, they walk with a cane, so they appear to have three legs.' When the monster heard this, she threw herself into the sea and died."

Contents of the Tomb

Inside the tomb are nineteen small stone chambers, each containing dozens of female corpses separated by thick plasterboards, arranged neatly and without disorder. Among the stone carvings, the statue of Pharaoh Ra is the most magnificent. Pharaoh Ra was the most outstanding high priest in Egypt during his lifetime. Other strangely shaped statues of gods evoke sighs from viewers. The leopard head stone carving is also worthy of admiration, with its eyes wide open and full of life. Outside the stone chambers is a long, deep passage with a large plaster column placed upside down, sculpted with the portraits of the senior priests' families. Pharaoh Ra's statue is also embedded in it. Another chamber, about 15 yards in circumference, has a stone pillar inscribed with Pharaoh Ra's life deeds and the circumstances of his funeral. The paintings are realistic and the carvings are exquisite. An inscription is engraved on the corner of the pillar, which is still not eroded. It was probably written by Pharaoh Ra's family. There are also many sacrifices and miscellaneous items scattered on the ground. Judging from the types of sacrifices, one can imagine Pharaoh Ra's hobbies and lifestyle during his lifetime.

The Treasures of the Tomb

Around Pharaoh Ra's statue are many plaster long-necked bottles. The tomb excavators initially did not understand their purpose, but when they entered the stone chamber, they were greeted by a fragrant smell that refreshed their minds and bodies, as if there were fresh flowers planted in the bottles. Only then did they realize that flowers had once been planted in the bottles. However, the fragrance remained after thousands of years. Many people suspect that there are medicines left in the bottles, which is probably a strange and suspicious case. Among these antiques, the most beautiful and moving is a very large gold flower vase. The gold is dazzling and radiant. The vase is filled with gold flower branches, making it even more luxurious. According to antique collectors, there have never been such precious Egyptian antiques since they were discovered. Among the many necklaces, one is made of four thousand rubies strung on a gold chain. Next to the necklace is a papyrus detailing the making of the necklace. It is said that this necklace was Pharaoh Ra's most cherished treasure during his lifetime. Later, when Pharaoh Ra married, he gave this treasure to his daughter-in-law as a greeting gift. (Opposite)

Stories of World Literature (I)(V)(VIII) Translated by Hu Zhongchi from American John Macy

Chapter 40 The Classical Era of German Literature

Gotthold Ephraim Lessing was a playwright, scholar, thinker, and critic. First of all, he wrote beautiful prose. He thought he lacked creative power, and as is often forgotten, he forgot that the great literary style itself is creation at the highest level. Some of his critical essays and theological pamphlets lack the reality of content today. This is the same fate that Lucian and Swift had. However, no critic of painting or poetry would dare to say that they do not know "Laocoön," and no critic or historian of drama would dare to say that they do not know "Hamburg Dramaturgy," and no researcher of thinkers would dare to say that they do not know "The Education of the Human Race" or "Fragments of the Wolfenbüttel Anonymous." The above works and other completely worthless works are valuable to those who love literature by virtue of that clear and brilliant talent, and eloquence, and the perfection of construction. Contact with Lessing's spirit, no matter how he handles the raw material, is called free education. Why? Because what Johnson wrote on Goldsmith's tombstone can be suitably applied to him: "There was no kind of writing that he did not attempt, and there was no writing that he touched that he did not adorn." One cannot speak of Lessing the playwright with the same respect, but rather more calmly. He gave the German people the first classical comedy in "Minna von Barnhelm" and the first poetic drama in high position in "Nathan the Wise." Both works are still popular on stage. However, "Minna von Barnhelm" has not faded at all, and even with "Nathan the Wise," it can be said that the highest value lies in the re-explanation of the author's noble, tolerant, and clear mind.

It is difficult to simply explain Goethe, the greatest of the German writers and one of the greatest figures in all of literature. He is the most modern figure among the greatest masters, and therefore the most complex in spirit, temperament, and activity. Dante represents the medieval worldview and cosmology, Shakespeare represents the moral order of the Renaissance, and Goethe does not represent anything. He is a modern man, one who seeks to make life crystallize into art. He is a first-rate lyric poet. "Faust" bears the same relationship to modern people as the Divine Comedy did to the people of the fourteenth century.

He is the author, and "Faust" expresses us - our times, problems, moral adventures, and is composed of letters, conversations, maxims, wind poems, rhymes, and prose maxims. It constitutes a vast range and permanent significance of the literature of wisdom, in which all the difficult problems and activities of the modern or scientific era are elaborated creatively with words that resonate with all educated people.

Art Guidelines

(1) Articles are limited to news, reviews, and introductions about the latest art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature at home and abroad.

(2) Pictures are limited to recent works by new domestic and foreign artists and illustrations related to the text.

(3) Photos are limited to recent portraits and works by domestic and foreign artists and various photographs related to the text.

(4) The number of words in each article should not exceed 3,000.

Republic of China, May 22, 1930 (Shen Bao

British Foreign Trade Increasingly Declining

Unprecedented Slump in Nine Years

Exports of All Major Commodities Decrease

Unemployment Rises Sharply to 1.6 Million

London News: British commerce continues to slump, with the situation in April being particularly bad, the worst since 1921 (excluding a certain month during the 1925 General Strike). Exports for the month were 47 million pounds, a decrease of 13 million pounds from the same period last year, or a decrease of 23 percent. Imports were 84 million pounds, a decrease of 20 million pounds from the same period last year, or a decrease of 20 percent. The reasons for this are partly due to the overall drop in special prices, partly due to the closure of wool mills, and partly due to the halt of Lancashire's cotton trade with India. But the main reason is the general slump, as the exports of all major ports have shrunk. This slump has increased the momentum of Lord Beaverbrook's Empire Free Trade movement, while protectionists are also quite active. Furthermore, British industry is exhausted, and unemployment is increasing. On April 28, the number reached 1.69 million, an increase of 38,000 from the previous two-week period and an increase of 530,000 from the same period last year.

Taiwan's Population at 4,550,000

An Increase of 110,000 from the Previous Year

Chinese Number 41,570

According to an investigation by the Taiwan Governor-General's Police Bureau, at the end of last year, the number of households in each state of the island was 288,086, the male population was 2,338,192, the female population was 2,218,269, totaling 4,556,461 people. Compared with the same period last year, the number of households increased by 49,047, and the population increased by 115,095. Among these were 10,054 households of Chinese, totaling 41,578 people. There were 63,353 households of Japanese, with 114,828 males and 100,965 females, totaling 215,793 people, an increase of 2,727 households and 9,781 people. There were 93 households of Koreans, totaling 565 people. Furthermore, in Taichung Prefecture, there were 804 households of Chinese, totaling 4,225 people, and 8,101 households of Japanese, totaling 26,872 people. The number of native island households was 159,288, totaling 970,329 people. There were 4 households of Koreans, totaling 62 people, and 7 households of foreigners, totaling 12 people.
